## v0.16.25 (Build 341) — 2026-07-15 — the native camera reaches the iPad/desktop chrome (and with it, iPad live camera over HDMI)

The first functional slice of the iPad/desktop camera lane (Daniel's spec): **on Capacitor, the desktop chrome's camera is now the NATIVE camera** — the same AVCaptureSession path the phone runs, swapped in on first camera entry when `host.nativeCamera.available` ([shell/source-host.js](../src/shell/source-host.js), lazy import so the desktop web bundle never carries @capacitor/core; the interface-compatible design meant the swap needed only four adaptations: a `flip()` shim on [native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js), a double-mirror guard + canvas-vs-video dims in `captureLiveFrame` (freeze would have silently failed on native — the RGB canvas has `width`, not `videoWidth`), and skipping the web-era saved-deviceId path). **This makes live camera over HDMI work on the iPad**: `env.liveCameraInfo` now carries the frame-socket `stream` info (port/mirror/acquisition gen), and the desktop HDMI sink sends the `native-camera` relay payload — the external view joins the socket as a second client, exactly the phone's proven path (B340's stream-generation re-post included, so flips/mode changes rebuild the receiver).

**Not yet in this build (queued next): the camera-settings GEAR** — on the iPad the native camera runs with its defaults (rear wide, auto EV/WB) and flip; lens/EV/WB/resolution get their desktop UI in the next increment (the settings-camera icons from B339 are its glyphs). Also explicitly deferred: iPad tap-to-focus + WB/EV gestures (a co-design round), the 48MP still-on-freeze for the desktop chrome, and the Electron-native camera backing.

Also filed to BACKLOG from Daniel's round: (1) the **iPad front-ultra-wide initial-load rotation repro** (90° CW + elongated staged preview, self-corrects on any camera switch — niche, documented, not blind-fixed); (2) **stabilization crop vs the future SVG overlay** (the uncropped full-res original is fine as long as the overlay SVG scales/positions against the true source aspect — a package-download follow-up); (3) **capture feedback honesty** (the white flash fires ~2s before the actual capture — the flash should ride the real capture moment, status should show simultaneously in both panels, and then the latency itself gets optimized).

## v0.16.24 (Build 340) — 2026-07-15 — record video no longer freezes the HDMI output (the stream-generation fix)

**Live camera over HDMI on the iPhone is CONFIRMED WORKING** (pass 7, the frame relay's first valid test) — and it exposed the last transition bug: switching to **record video froze the external display on the last live frame** (state still streamed — his slice gestures moved out there — but the source didn't follow), unrecovered by switching back to live camera, recovered by going still-then-live. Root cause: record video **re-acquires the camera** (video format/fps), which restarts the frame socket and kills the external receiver's connection — but the source SIGNATURE (`cam:native:<facing>`) didn't change, so the external view never rebuilt its receiver (and the receiver deliberately doesn't auto-reconnect: the still→live dance worked because the signature changed twice). Fix: [native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js) tracks a **stream generation** (bumps per acquisition) and reports it in `streamInfo()`; the mobile source signature includes it, so ANY re-acquire (flip, still/video mode, resolution, fps) re-posts the source and the external view rebuilds its receiver on the fresh stream. During the transition the external view honestly shows black + hint (streamInfo is null mid-acquire), then the new stream lands.

## v0.16.23 (Build 339) — 2026-07-15 — camera UX cleanup: capture/live-camera copy + the settings-camera icons

Daniel's non-functional cleanup ahead of the iPad/desktop camera lane:

- **The desktop shutter says what it does.** Live shows pause bars + **"capture"** (pressing it captures this frame); frozen shows the green dot + **"live camera"** (pressing it goes back live). Replaces "pause"/"live", whose verbs described the mechanism, not the intent. [shell/source-host.js](../src/shell/source-host.js).
- **The camera-settings icon is now a settings icon.** The plain camera glyph read as "the camera," not "camera settings" (his call). Two Google Material glyphs (Daniel-supplied as design intent, adapted into the icon set's conventions like `captureCam` — 960-grid wrap, currentColor): **gear+photo-camera** in still capture, **gear+video-camera** in record video, swapped mode-aware on the mobile camera-menu button. The same glyphs are reserved for the coming desktop camera-settings gear. [mobile/icons.js](../src/mobile/icons.js), [mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js).

Pass-6 device results also recorded here: **iPhone stills over HDMI work** (the probe fix held; output settles ~1080p-class at his canvas aspect); iPad stills great; both live-camera hints behave as designed; **iPad web-camera source showed 90° CW rotated in the source panel** — a NEW watch item, not blind-fixed (need to know: does it rotate without HDMI connected too?). The iPhone native-cam live-over-HDMI test was invalidated by the B338 flag regression — it re-runs on the next build, now flag-proof.

## v0.16.22 (Build 338) — 2026-07-15 — the native camera is now the Capacitor DEFAULT (the lost-camera-menu regression)

Daniel's high-pri report: recent device builds lost the native camera controls (the camera menu with lens/EV/WB reverted to the bare flip icon). Root cause was procedural, not code: the native camera was still gated behind the `VITE_FOLD_NATIVE_CAM` build flag, and **every plain `vite build && cap sync` run during the HDMI lane silently overwrote the iOS bundle with the web-camera build** — his Xcode runs then shipped it. (This also means the iPhone live-camera-over-HDMI tests never exercised the native path — the frame-socket relay is still untested.) The fix removes the failure mode instead of patching it: **`useNativeCam` is now simply `host.nativeCamera.available`** — a capability the host reports should never depend on a build flag. This is the "flip the default" decision parked at the camera close-out, now made (his call). Web builds are unaffected (`host.nativeCamera.available` is false off-device). The `native:cam` npm script is gone — **`npm run ios` is THE build**. [mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js), [package.json](../package.json).

## v0.16.21 (Build 337) — 2026-07-15 — the iPhone crash's true root cause (the engine probe bomb) + the dual-capture verdict

Pass 5 cracked both remaining problems, and the iPhone one was ours all along:

- **The external view was jetsam-killed by the ENGINE'S BOOT PROBE, not the render size.** His log showed the web process dying between `loaded` and `hello` at every degradation step — size-independent, so B336's adaptive caps couldn't save it. Root cause: `createEngine` without `maxProbeSize` walks FBO probe sizes up to `maxTextureSize` and deliberately COMMITS the memory — on the iPhone that's a **~1GB 16384² attempt** inside a memory-tight webview. The mobile chrome has capped its probe (4096) since forever for exactly this reason; [output-view.js](../src/output-view.js) never passed a cap. It now probes at most **2048** (this view only renders to canvas — it never exports, so it needs no big FBO at all). This was very likely the root of the whole crash saga: pass-3's landscape loop, pass-4's instant deaths, and the marginal-memory GPU crashes around it. The B336 breaker + degradation stay as the safety net they were meant to be. Lesson banked in memory: every engine in an embedded/secondary iOS webview must cap its probe.
- **The dual-getUserMedia verdict is in: dead end, and actively harmful.** On the iPad the facingMode fix got the second capture GRANTED — and iOS then starved both: ~1 frame per 5–15s on the external screen and the main source/preview panels went dark. So the web-camera-over-HDMI attempt is retired on the native transport (both chromes now send an honest hint instead — stills broadcast fine; the desktop popup path on macOS keeps its proven dual capture). **Live camera over HDMI = the frame-relay architecture only** (the native camera's multi-client socket — already shipped for the iPhone's native build, untested while the view was crash-looping; the probe fix unblocks that test). **For the iPad, live-camera-over-HDMI now waits on bringing the native camera to the iPad/desktop chrome — a decision item for Daniel in BACKLOG** (it would also bring EV/WB/48MP stills to the iPad).

Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync` (JS-only build). Device-pending pass 6 (the probe fix should make it short): iPhone still in portrait AND landscape at full native res (no crash expected now), iPhone native-cam live camera over HDMI (the frame socket's first fair test), iPad still + the honest camera hint.

## v0.16.20 (Build 336) — 2026-07-15 — HDMI pass 4: crash-loop breaker, adaptive size degradation, the cross-origin camera fix

Daniel's pass-4 logs (the iPad session + a 5868-line iPhone record) turned the remaining mysteries into three diagnosed bugs:

- **The iPhone "landscape flicker" was a CRASH-RELOAD LOOP — 113 cycles.** The external view's web process died under memory pressure (landscape sizes the phone's own canvases larger; the external webview is the freshest big allocation, so jetsam kills it first), and B335's auto-reload re-allocated straight into the same wall — each reload flashed the "connecting…" hint he saw. Two-sided fix: **(1) a breaker in the plugin** — more than 3 deaths in a minute tears the window down entirely and reports `crashLoop`, so **iOS falls back to mirroring the device** (the projector still shows something; unplug/replug or a manual start resets the budget); **(2) adaptive degradation in the poster** — each crash steps the external render size down (display-native → 1920 → 1280 long edge) and the still data-URL cap with it (4096 → 2048 → 1280), re-posting the smaller source to the fresh view, reset per plug session. 4K where the device can, smaller where it can't, and the console says which.
- **The iPad's "no device found amongst 5 devices" was the cross-origin deviceId bug.** getUserMedia deviceIds are salted PER ORIGIN — the main webview's id can never match inside the `fold-ext://` external view, so its `deviceId:{exact}` constraint failed against all 5 devices. The camera payload over the native transport now sends **facingMode + negotiated dims instead of deviceId** (both chromes), and [output-view.js](../src/output-view.js) retries a failed deviceId by facingMode — the same-origin popup path keeps its deviceId behavior. Whether iOS then permits the second concurrent capture on iPad is the remaining device question; failure now degrades to the hint, not constraint churn.
- The iPad's mid-session GPU-process crash (`GPUProcessProxy::gpuProcessExited: reason=Crash` — the "app auto-corrected with a new session") confirmed B335's recovery firing (`PiP RESTORED` in his log). The pressure sources it pointed at — the failed-constraint churn and the external view's footprint — are both reduced by the fixes above.

Also: `docs/temp/` gitignored (device-log scratch space). Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim **BUILD SUCCEEDED**. Device-pending pass 5: landscape still (expect at most a couple of reload blinks, then either stability at a smaller size or a clean fall-back to mirroring), iPad live camera (facingMode should get past constraints — the dual-capture question gets its real answer), iPhone native-cam live camera over HDMI.

## v0.16.19 (Build 335) — 2026-07-15 — GL context-loss auto-recovery everywhere (the HDMI regression pass)

Daniel's third device pass regressed hard: plugging into the 4K monitor **killed the MAIN window's WebGL** on iPad ("graphics context lost — reload to recover", staged + live panels gray; reproducible on relaunch), and the iPhone stopped outputting stills. The diagnosis: **iOS may drop an app's GL contexts when a display attaches** (GPU reconfiguration/memory pressure — the external view's web content process can also be killed outright), and our recovery coverage was asymmetric — the **mobile chrome** has had full `engine.reinitGL()` restore since the save-handoff bug, but the **desktop shell (which the iPad runs) had none**: main.js only logged and showed a "reload to recover" message that is meaningless in a native app (Daniel's exact point). Once the external webview died on the iPhone, nothing healed it either — every source after showed black.

Recovery is now wired at every GL surface, using the engine's existing `reinitGL()` (rebuilds all GPU resources on the same context object and re-uploads the source):

- **Desktop preview engine** ([main.js](../src/main.js)): status shows "recovering…" on loss; on restore → `reinitGL()` + re-render + the message clears.
- **Live PiP engine** ([perform-runtime.js](../src/shell/perform-runtime.js)): restore → `reinitGL()` + source resync next tick.
- **Output-bus hidden engine** ([output-engine.js](../src/shell/output-engine.js)): the restore handler reset the source but never rebuilt the GPU resources — now it does.
- **The external/popup view** ([output-view.js](../src/output-view.js)): runs unattended, so it must self-heal — restore → `reinitGL()` + a fresh `hello` so the driver re-posts the source; losses are reported upstream (`glLost`/`glRestored` in the device console).
- **External web-process death** (the permanent-black case): the plugin now implements `webViewWebContentProcessDidTerminate` → reloads output.html + reports `crashed`; the poster re-posts the source on the fresh view's hello.

Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim **BUILD SUCCEEDED**. Device-pending: the console will now say exactly what happens at plug-in (expect `WebGL context LOST/RESTORED (preview canvas)` on iPad with the panels healing themselves; `crashed`/`glLost` lines from the external view on iPhone if pressure killed it). If losses prove chronic at attach time, the next lever is capping the external view's render size on phones — with data, not preemptively.

## v0.16.18 (Build 334) — 2026-07-15 — the live native camera reaches the external display + the fill-display toggle

Daniel's second device pass: stills over HDMI work on BOTH devices (the scene-wait fix landed); the remaining gap was **live camera / record video never reaching the external screen** — and a stale still persisting there when the source switched to one the external view couldn't open. Three pieces this build:

- **The native camera now broadcasts to the external display via a SECOND frame-socket client.** Camera frames can't cross WKWebViews, and iOS won't grant a second capture session — but the native camera already streams biplanar YUV over a localhost WebSocket, so the fix is architectural, not a workaround: `FrameSocketServer.swift` goes **multi-client** (per-client send state; a slow client drops frames without stalling a fast one; the encode still skips when nobody's ready), and the external view joins as a receive-only consumer. New [shell/native-camera-receiver.js](../src/shell/native-camera-receiver.js) (plain WebSocket + WebGL2, no Capacitor dep, 1 kB lazy chunk) decodes the same wire format; the YUV→RGB blitter is **extracted verbatim** to [shell/yuv-renderer.js](../src/shell/yuv-renderer.js) (the kit/drift.js precedent — one proven implementation, two consumers; [native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js) now imports it and exposes `streamInfo()`). The mobile chrome's source payload sends `{ kind:'native-camera', port, mirror }`; a camera flip re-posts (facing rides the signature) so the selfie mirror follows. **Record video inherits it** — the external screen streams the followed look while the follower chases.
- **Stale-frame fix** (his repro: load a still → switch to live camera → the still persists out there): `teardownSource` in [output-view.js](../src/output-view.js) now **clears the canvas** — black + the hint is the honest in-between while a source loads or when it fails, on the external display and the desktop popup alike.
- **The fill-display toggle** (his ask): default stays FIT (the canvas frame aspect out there, WYSIWYG with recording/save); FILL renders edge-to-edge at the display's native aspect (the installation case). `session.hdmiFill`, live-toggleable mid-broadcast (the poster recomputes dims per tick; the external view resizes on the next message). Desktop: a "fill display" toggle beside the destination picker, visible when HDMI is selected ([index.html](../index.html) + [output-panel.js](../src/shell/output-panel.js)). Mobile: a fit-canvas/fill-display segment in canvas settings, shown where the host can present an external display ([mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js)).

The web-path camera on the external view (iPad, second getUserMedia of the same device) remains device-pending — if iOS refuses it, the iPad's live-camera-over-HDMI answer is the native camera path once that flag flips. Verified: `node --check` all touched files; `vite build` (default + native-cam variant) clean; `cap sync`; `xcodebuild` sim **BUILD SUCCEEDED** (the multi-client server compiles). Runtime device-pending.

## v0.16.17 (Build 333) — 2026-07-15 — HDMI device-pass fixes: iPhone black screen (scene-wait) + honor the canvas aspect

Daniel's first HDMI device pass (4K Dell via USB-C adapter): **iPad works beautifully; iPhone drove the display (backlight on) but composited nothing.** Root cause fits all observations: the system's `UIWindowScene` for an external screen arrives slightly AFTER `UIScreen.didConnectNotification`. The iPad worked because a human pressed start seconds later (scene existed → clean attach); the iPhone's autoconnect attached within milliseconds → no scene yet → the plugin fell into the deprecated `window.screen` path, which on a modern iPhone drives the signal but composites nothing. **Fix:** `start()` now WAITS for the matching scene (250ms polling, 3s deadline — notification delivery isn't guaranteed in AppDelegate compatibility mode) and only then presents; past the deadline it falls back to the classic assignment and REPORTS it. **Diagnostics added so the next console run is conclusive:** status carries `attach: "scene" | "classic"`; the webview's navigation delegate reports `loaded` / `loadError` events; the JS poster logs hello / loaded / loadError / the attach path (`⚡️ [info] [fold] external view …` in the Xcode console).

**The canvas aspect is now honored on the external display** (his iPad note: a 4:5 portrait canvas rendered as 16:9 out there — inconsistent with the canvas/recording/save, which all honor `frameAspect`). The poster fits the frame aspect inside the display's native pixels — full sharpness at that aspect, letterboxed by the view's object-fit — via a `getFrameAspect` opt both chromes supply. A "fill the display" toggle is a cheap follow-up if the installation case wants edge-to-edge.

Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim **BUILD SUCCEEDED**. Device-pending: the iPhone re-test (expect `attach: scene` and a picture; if it still blacks out with `attach: classic` + `loaded`, the next step is adopting a scene manifest — a known, contained change).

## v0.16.16 (Build 332) — 2026-07-15 — HDMI autoconnect on the iPhone (mobile chrome)

**Plug the phone into HDMI and the program presents on the external screen automatically** — no picker, no arm step (Daniel's call: one display, one intent; the mobile chrome has no destinations UI). Unplug and it stops. [shell/external-display.js](../src/shell/external-display.js) refactored into a shared **poster core** (plugin lifecycle + the per-frame state stream + source sync) with two thin consumers: `createExternalDisplaySink` (the desktop-chrome destination, unchanged behavior) and `createExternalDisplayAutoconnect` (the mobile behavior). [mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js) wires autoconnect at boot (lazy import, `host.externalDisplay.available`-gated) and supplies the program accessor: **the external screen shows the FOLLOWED look while record-video's follower chases** (`lastEased` — what the recording captures), the working state otherwise — so what goes out over HDMI is always what the audience/recording sees, never the raw edit preview mid-ease.

Source support on the phone this pass: stills (frozen captures + uploads, as data URLs — fresh objects per freeze, so reference-identity re-posts work) and the web-path live camera (deviceId from the live track; the external view opens its own capture — device-pending). The **native camera feed can't cross webviews yet** (its frames ride a single-client socket); the external view shows an honest hint until you capture a still — the follow-up is a second client on the frame socket. Verified: `node --check`, `vite build` (the shared module is a 4.1 kB lazy chunk), `cap sync`; no native code changed this build. Runtime device-pending.

## v0.16.15 (Build 331) — 2026-07-15 — HDMI out (Capacitor iPad/desktop chrome): the external display joins the destination picker

**Plug an iPad (or any Capacitor build running the full app) into HDMI and the chrome-free program view presents on the external screen** — the arc's "standalone activation broadcasting out." This is Lane 3's HDMI lane riding directly on Lane 4A: the external view renders **from the committed program state-stream** (`env.programState`, now the committed frame), not captured pixels — zero readback, the display's native resolution, works from every mode (still edits live, motion's committed loop while staging, perform's follower-eased output while the device screen keeps the stage).

The pieces:

- **`native-plugins/fold-external-display`** (new local plugin, the DISTRIBUTION.md pattern): watches `UIScreen` connect/disconnect (one external display at a time on iOS — no picker needed), presents a second `UIWindow` + WKWebView loading `output.html`, and bridges per-frame state via `evaluateJavaScript` into `window.__foldExternal` (BroadcastChannel can't cross WKWebViews). A tiny **`fold-ext://` scheme handler** serves the bundled web assets — the bridge's `capacitor://` handler belongs to the main webview's configuration, and `file://` breaks ES modules (null origin). Messages travel up (hello/fps) via a script message handler → plugin events. A `WKUIDelegate` grants the external view's getUserMedia (our own content; the app holds the camera permission — the prompt can't present on a screen without input). **iOS exposes no product name for the display** — status reports resolution; JS labels it.
- **[shell/external-display.js](../src/shell/external-display.js)** — the sink (sibling of output-window.js, transport swapped): posts the committed program frame per tick + the source payload on change; registered as `{ id:'hdmi', needsBus:false }` (self-rendering — never starts the bus readback loop). Lazy chunk (the native-camera pattern) so the web bundle stays clean. Renders at the **display's native resolution** when known.
- **[output-view.js](../src/output-view.js)** — dual ingress (BroadcastChannel + `__foldExternal`), `sendUp` up-channel, stills as **data URLs** (ImageBitmap can't cross the bridge; capped at 4096 long edge), and an honest `unsupported` hint payload.
- **[output-panel.js](../src/shell/output-panel.js)** — `env.addOutputDestination` (late registration: native modules load async), **auto-select on plug-in** (connecting a display IS the intent — Daniel's call), and clean state recovery when the display is yanked mid-broadcast.

**Source support this build:** stills (data URL) + live camera (the external view opens its own capture of the same device — the proven desktop-popup pattern; whether iOS allows the second concurrent capture is DEVICE-PENDING, fallback = a second client on the native camera's frame socket). **Video sources deferred** (blob URLs are per-context; follow-up = serve the clip through the asset scheme). **iPhone mobile-chrome autoconnect is the next increment** (no destinations UI there — plug in and it streams).

Verified: `node --check` all touched files; `vite build` clean (external-display is a 3.3 kB lazy chunk); `cap sync` integrates the plugin (5 plugins, `packageClassList` + Package.swift); `xcodebuild` sim **BUILD SUCCEEDED**. Runtime is device-pending (Daniel's iPad + a USB-C/HDMI adapter).

## v0.16.14 (Build 330) — 2026-07-15 — the program-snapshot discipline (Lane 4A)

**Every output destination now reads a COMMITTED program snapshot instead of the live mutable `state`.** This is the Capacitor arc's Lane 4A — the architectural prerequisite for HDMI broadcast (the external WKWebView needs a committed state-stream; BroadcastChannel can't cross web views) and iOS native capture. It replaces the "two-loop shared-state" bug class (BACKLOG: a slice drag during playback once leaked a transient uncommitted edit into the Syphon broadcast — Build 201 — and each new real-time writer like the control bus multiplied the ways that could recur) with one rule: **a single writer commits an immutable param snapshot at a defined point per frame; consumers read committed frames only.**

Two new files, mechanism/payload split for the future shared package (reviewed as an independent API-architecture pass at Daniel's ask before building):

- [stage/commit-cell.js](../src/stage/commit-cell.js) — the generic mechanism: a single-writer, latest-value cell `{ value, gen, t }`; value is opaque (no kaleidoscope knowledge), `gen` bumps only when the committed value actually changes, `t` marks when the look went on air. This is the piece Lane 4C extracts; a future tenant (tap, zoetrope) commits its own payload, and a signal-heavy tool can run a second cell. Deliberately control-rate (once per presentable look), not an audio-rate signal path.
- [shell/program-frame.js](../src/shell/program-frame.js) — Fold's instance: value = the param snapshot; owns the presentable-look precedence (perform follower ?? motion staging's committed loop ?? working state — moved verbatim from perform-runtime) and the two commit regimes: **automation owns the frame** (motion playback/scrub, perform, staging, the take blend — those loops call `env.commitFrame()` right after producing the look; a read between ticks can never catch a manual transient) and **manual modes** (no automation owns the state, so the live look IS the program by definition — reads commit on demand, zero added latency, and a missed commit point can never freeze a broadcast).

Commit points wired: `scheduleRender` ([main.js](../src/main.js)), motion playback (`renderSampled`), video playback tick, scrub loop, `stgLoop`, `stgBlendLoop` ([motion-runtime.js](../src/shell/motion-runtime.js)), the perform tick ([perform-runtime.js](../src/shell/perform-runtime.js), which no longer defines `programState` itself). `env.programState()` keeps its exact signature — all four consumers ([output-engine.js](../src/shell/output-engine.js), [output-window.js](../src/shell/output-window.js), the bus via [fold-adapter.js](../src/shell/fold-adapter.js), the perform PiP) work unchanged, now reading committed values. The motion edit lock stays as belt-and-suspenders (Daniel's call — relax later once the model is proven). The frame governs **params only**; source-pixel freshness (texture upload, the seek guard) stays each consumer's separate concern. Undo/redo untouched (the frame is a read-side copy, never a second source of truth).

Naming per Daniel's review round: `programFrame` (read) / `commitFrame` (write) — "commit" kept deliberately (the transactional "this look is now the program," matching staging's "committed copy" vocabulary; "update" would undersell it and collide with `updateSourceFrame`). Simplification found in review: the video clock was dropped from the frame (the proposal had scoped the snapshot to params and then contradicted itself); `videoSync` stays consumer-side, unchanged.

Verified: a 16-assertion node logic harness over the real modules (mock env; proves manual commit-on-read + gen dedupe, perform/staging/playback transient-blocking, precedence, snapshot immutability, unchanged-look stability) — 16/16; `node --check` on all touched files; `vite build` clean. Behavior-neutral by design for all shipping paths. Proposal + review record: `docs/PROPOSAL-program-snapshot.md`.

## v0.16.13 (Build 329) — 2026-07-14 — video stabilization (fixes the shaky low-level feed)

**Low-level camera capture defaults stabilization OFF** (WebKit/getUserMedia had it on), which made the native feed shakier than the old web path. The plugin now sets `preferredVideoStabilizationMode` on the video connection (gated on active-format support): **`.standard` for still-compose** (light crop), **`.cinematicExtended` for video-record** (max smoothing). Video-record needs nothing else — the recorded output samples the stabilized preview directly. **Stills need a crop-match:** stabilization crops the *video* stream, but the 48MP still comes from the photo output, which isn't video-stabilized — so the still is the wider full sensor and would shift the composition on capture. [mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js) `freezeFromUrl` now **center-crops the still to the stabilized FOV** by a per-mode factor the plugin reports ([shell/native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js) `getStillCropFactor`). **Caveat:** AVFoundation doesn't expose the exact stabilization crop (it's dynamic), so the factors are ESTIMATES (`standard: 0.9`, `cinematicExtended: 0.76`, …) — tunable in one JS map, **calibrate on device** (when the still FOV doesn't quite match the composed preview, nudge the factor). The saved-package "original" stays the full uncropped file. Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED. Device-pending.

## v0.16.12 (Build 328) — 2026-07-13 — delete the camera frame-bridge spike (native path proven)

**The throwaway harness is gone.** The Tier-2 frame-bridge spike (`src/spike/camera-spike.js` + the `VITE_FOLD_SPIKE=camera` boot gate + the `spike:camera` npm script) measured native-camera→WebSocket→WebGL feasibility on device; the real path graduated and is now feature-complete, so it's removed. [boot.js](../src/boot.js) drops the spike branch (the app boot is no longer wrapped in an else); the native camera plugin (`native-plugins/fold-native-camera`) — the keeper — stays. Verified: `vite build` (default + native) clean, no dangling references. No behavior change.

**Record-video now captures audio on the native camera path.** The native camera is video-only (no audio track to clone, unlike the web camera's getUserMedia stream), so [mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js) acquires the mic via `getUserMedia({audio})` **at record-video entry** — one clean permission prompt at mode entry rather than mid-record — holds it for the session, and clones a track into each take (so a recorder's stop doesn't kill the held mic). Released on leaving record-video. Denial degrades to video-only. **Architecture note:** native plugin-captured audio can't join a JS `<canvas>`-captured recording (the take is the WebGL output, recorded in JS), so getUserMedia IS the correct native-app audio path — WKWebView supports it, and the mic usage string is already in Info.plist. Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`. Device-pending (confirm a recorded take has audio).

**Tap the source on the native live camera to focus + re-meter at that point**, with a focus ring for feedback. A quick tap (distinct from the press-hold EV/WB pad and from a slice drag — same classifier) calls the plugin's new `setFocusPoint`, which sets `focusPointOfInterest` + `exposurePointOfInterest` and one-shot `autoFocus`, leaving the user's manual EV bias / WB untouched. The screen→sensor coordinate map is rotation-aware (uses the RotationCoordinator angle) and un-mirrors the front camera. [plugin] `setFocusPoint`; [shell/native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js) + [mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js) (`tapFocus` wired into the pad's tap branch; `#m-focus-ring`). **The coordinate mapping is a first cut** — the focus ring shows where you tapped, but the exact sensor point may need one on-device calibration pass (the rotation transform is the uncertain part). Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED. Device-pending.

Two fixes from Daniel's first video-record test this arc:

- **Video save now works.** The save mechanism was fine for stills but silently failed for video: [shell/capacitor-host.js](../src/shell/capacitor-host.js) `save()` base64-encoded the *entire* blob into one string and shipped it over the JS→native bridge in a single call — OK for a ~5MB still, a silent failure for a tens-to-hundreds-of-MB video. It now **writes in 3MB chunks** (`writeFile` then `appendFile`; the slice size is a multiple of 3 bytes so base64 chunks concatenate cleanly). Also, `downloadBlob` now returns its promise and the video-save actions **await it and surface failures** ([mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js)) instead of swallowing them.
- **No more 4K60 crash.** The 14 Pro can *natively* do 4K60, but not while also running our capture→YUV→RGB→engine→encode pipeline. A **scalable capability gate** (Daniel's heuristic): the device's PEAK resolution×fps combo is excluded, everything below is offered — so the 14 Pro gets 4K→30, 1080p→30/60, and a device that can sustain more is gated less, all off what the plugin reports (per-resolution max fps + dims). [shell/native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js) `safeFps` computes it and clamps the actual `targetFps` (so a stale 60 can't leak into a 4K record); the menu's fps row consumes it.

Also filed the imprecise "sharp output up to ~XK" save hint to BACKLOG (order-of-magnitude SWAG, hardening later — Daniel's call). Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED. Device-pending.

**Fix:** the full-res capture lost the user's exposure/white-balance adjustments. Switching `device.activeFormat` to the photo format (for the 48MP shot) resets the device to auto EV/WB, so the still came out with the default look, not the preview's. [plugin] `capturePhoto` now **snapshots the current exposure bias + (locked) WB gains before the switch and re-applies them after**, and — since exposure needs a beat to settle on the new format — fires the shot after a short (0.18s) delay when a switch happened. **Also:** the save-sheet diagnostics now show the **source resolution** ([mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js)) — useful on its own, and the datum needed to calibrate the "sharp output up to ~XK" hint (which Daniel flagged as undercounting; the hint formula multiplies slice-source-detail × mirror-tiles × a 0.5 softening and currently ignores the canvas aspect — pending his form/settings to fix precisely). Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED. Device-pending.

Three fixes from Daniel's 14 Pro pass on the full-res still path:

- **Capture no longer shifts the composition.** The preview streamed the 16:9 light video format while the capture used the 4:3 photo format — different fields of view, so the framing jumped on pause and had to be re-composed. Still mode now previews with a **light format matching the photo aspect** (4:3, same FOV); video mode keeps 16:9. [plugin] `configureSession` gained a `stillMode` path that picks a light aspect-matched format; `preferPhoto` retired.
- **The engine now samples the FULL-resolution still**, not a 4096 downsample. Daniel's point: downsampling a still the user chose at 48MP is dishonest, and the high-res source is exactly what gives compositional freedom (crop hard, still get sharp output). The 4096 engine-source cap is gone; instead the **still-resolution picker is gated by the GPU's max texture size** ([mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js) `refreshCamMenu`) — we only offer a size the device can actually hold, and drop to the largest allowed if the current pick exceeds it. The full-res file remains the saved original. (Export resolution was already GPU-probe-gated up to 8192+.)
- **Save honors the canvas aspect** (was always square). `doSave` never passed `session.frameAspect` to `engine.exportAt`, whose `aspect` defaults to 1 — a mobile-save omission, not Capacitor-specific. Now it passes the aspect and reports the true `w×h`.

Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED. **Device-pending (watch the memory on full-res 48MP, and confirm the aspect-matched preview eliminates the shift).**

**The right fix for 48MP without the heavy preview.** The live preview stays on the light 1080p video format (from B320, so no crash/lag); at **capture time** the plugin switches the active format to the full photo format, captures at the chosen size (up to the sensor's max — e.g. 48MP), and the shell stops the session right after (the next go-live starts fresh on the light format — no switch-back). Preview frames are dropped during the switch (a `capturing` flag) so the brief heavy format streams nothing, and the shell stops rendering the preview before the capture — so the switch is invisible, no burst. The camera menu's still-resolution row now reports the **PHOTO format's** real sizes (12MP / 48MP) rather than the light preview format's caps (the 2/10MP Daniel saw). One guard: the engine samples a **4096-capped working copy** of the still (mobile output is bounded there anyway, and a 48MP RGBA texture ≈195MB would risk the OOM we just fixed) while the **full-resolution file is kept as the saved original**. [plugin] `bestPhotoFormat` + capture-time `beginConfiguration`/`activeFormat` switch + `capturing` frame-drop; [mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js) `freezeFromUrl` size-cap. Falls back to the preview-frame freeze on any failure. Flag-gated; device-pending. Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED.

**Two refinements from Daniel's 14 Pro pass.** (1) **WB range widened to 2000–9000K** — auto white balance settles *below* the old 2500 floor in warm light (he measured 2331), so the live slider clamped to 2500 while showing an auto value beneath it; the manual range now covers where auto actually goes. (2) **Gesture pad locks to one axis** — he found himself subconsciously avoiding diagonals and wanting *either* EV or WB, not both at once. The pad now locks to the dominant axis on the first real move (vertical → EV, horizontal → WB) and the HUD shows just that value; a fresh press re-picks. [plugin] `temperatureMin/Max`; [mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js) pad `padAxis`. Flag-gated; device-pending. Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED.

**Watch item (not fixed):** brief color banding at camera start — red/blue on the 14 Pro, a green vertical band once on the 17 Pro — transient and self-resolving. Likely a first-frame / texture-upload glitch in the YUV→RGB path (echoes an old mobile-Safari timeline banding). Left as a watch item per Daniel; revisit if it stops self-resolving.

**Regression from B316, caught on the 14 Pro.** Making still mode use the photo-optimized format meant the live preview streamed the format's huge native frames (`4032×3024` = 12MP) through YUV→RGB→engine every frame — ~24× the pixels of the old 1080p preview — which OOM-crashed the GPU/web-content process (`GPUProcessProxy` / `WebProcessProxy` crash in Daniel's log) and degraded fps in both panels. The capture never fired before the crash; it was purely the heavy live preview. **Fix:** [shell/native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js) now always starts with `preferPhoto: false` — a light 1080p **video** format previews smoothly (restoring the slices-1–5 feel) and still captures ~12MP stills on pause (video formats cap stills there, which is all the 14 Pro offered anyway). This also fixes a dims-mismatch (the photo format delivered 4032×3024 frames while the session reported 1920×1080). **Tradeoff:** the full 48MP on capable devices (e.g. 17 Pro) now needs a capture-time format switch rather than a permanently heavy preview — a designed follow-up, not shipped here (stability first). Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED; **device-pending Daniel's confirm the crash + lag are gone.**

**Daniel's press-hold gesture, a testable first cut.** Press-hold anywhere in the source (still for 450ms) on the native live camera engages a pad: drag **Y = exposure** (up brighter), **X = white balance** (warm right) — his axes — with a centered HUD showing the live values. A quick move stays a **slice drag** (untouched); a quick tap is reserved for **tap-to-focus** (deferred: its screen→sensor map depends on the just-changed orientation, so it's wired after that's confirmed). Built as an **additive, fenced** capture-phase listener on `#m-source` ([mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js)) that only stops propagation to the slice overlay ONCE the hold engages — so slice manipulation is untouched otherwise, and **no `overlay.js` change**. Active only on the native live camera (`useNativeCam` + `cameraMode === 'live'`), so blast radius is the native path. This is the surface Daniel flagged for hands-on tuning — expect the hold time, sensitivity, and tap/focus to iterate. Flag-gated; device-pending. Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED.

**The native frame (and the still) now stays horizon-level in every rotation.** The old path baked a fixed 90° into the capture, so the rear camera was only upright in portrait (Daniel's rule: rotate left → image rotated right, and vice-versa — the "capture fixed, not tracking the device" signature), and the front was 90°-off even in portrait. Rather than hand-roll per-orientation angle math (sign-error-prone, and I can't runtime-verify it here), the plugin uses **`AVCaptureDevice.RotationCoordinator`** (iOS 17+) — Apple's sanctioned API that computes the correct capture angle for the current device orientation *and* sensor (front included, so it also fixes the front offset) and updates as the device turns via KVO. Both the video-data and photo connections track it, so the preview and a captured still rotate together. Pre-iOS-17 falls back to fixed portrait. [plugin] `setupRotationCoordinator`/`applyRotation`; no JS changes needed (self-updating natively). Flag-gated; device-pending — **if live rotation doesn't update, the first thing to try is creating the coordinator on the main queue** (it observes device orientation). Verified: `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED.

**The crude auto/manual toggle is gone.** Per Daniel's 17 Pro feedback, white balance is now a single always-visible Kelvin slider: in **auto** it tracks the live temperature the camera has settled on (the plugin reads the current `deviceWhiteBalanceGains` → temperature, polled ~600ms while the menu is open); **dragging** it commits to manual; **tapping the value** (`5200K · auto`, which doubles as the affordance) returns to auto. New plugin `getWhiteBalance`; [shell/native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js) `readWhiteBalanceTemp`; [mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js) `buildCamWb` rewritten with a self-terminating poll (stops on close / manual / hide) and the menu-open handler now refreshes to restart it. Flag-gated; device-pending. Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED.

**The minor bump marks the native iOS camera as a real feature** (Daniel's call) — flip, physical-lens picker, per-lens resolution, EV/WB, and now full-resolution still capture, all through a native AVCaptureSession streaming into the engine. This build makes the resolution picker **mode-aware and the still capture real:**

- **Record-video mode:** the resolution row is video sizes — **1080p / QHD / 4K** (720p dropped: never record below 1080p; QHD self-hides on devices without a 1440p format).
- **Still mode (live camera):** the resolution row now shows the sensor's actual **photo sizes (12MP / 48MP, etc.)** — read from the active photo format's `supportedMaxPhotoDimensions`, not the video sizes it wrongly showed before. Still mode configures a photo-optimized format so the sensor's full still is reachable; picking a size just sets the next capture's dimensions (no re-acquire — the preview keeps streaming).
- **Pause = a real high-res capture:** on pause in still mode, `capturePhoto` fires at the chosen size, writes a JPEG to a temp file, and the engine loads it (via `Capacitor.convertFileSrc`) as the editable source — replacing the old preview-res freeze. The photo connection's rotation matches the preview; the front-camera selfie mirror is re-applied in JS; a shutter flash gives feedback. Falls back to the preview-frame freeze on record-video, the web camera, or any failure. The still is NOT auto-saved to Photos — it's the source; the user saves the edited result through the export flow.

[plugin] reports `stillResolutions` + `capturePhoto` takes per-shot dimensions and returns a file URL. [shell/native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js) gains `setStillMode`/`setStillResolution`/`getStillResolutions` + the convertFileSrc round-trip. [mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js) splits `captureFrame` into the native high-res path + the preview fallback. Flag-gated; device-pending Daniel's 14 Pro pass. Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED.

---

## v0.15.14 (Build 315) — 2026-07-12 — camera slice 5: EV + white-balance sliders (capability-driven, reset on lens switch)

**The manual controls the native camera exists for.** Under the resolution rows, the camera menu now has an **exposure** slider (EV bias across the device's reported `exposureBias` range, live) and a **white balance** control — an auto/manual toggle, and in manual a **Kelvin temperature** slider (2500–8000K, the plugin clamps the gains). Both drive the device-proven plugin methods (`setExposureBias`, `setWhiteBalance`). The WB manual row only appears where the physical lens supports custom gains — which it does now that production always drives a physical lens (the whole reason we dropped "auto"). **Reset semantics (Daniel's call):** EV/WB reset on a lens or facing change (a different physical sensor — per-sensor gains don't carry), but are **kept across a resolution/fps change** (same sensor) — [shell/native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js) resets on flip/`setLens` and re-applies the persisted values after any re-acquire, so a resolution switch doesn't wipe your exposure. [mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js) gains `buildCamSlider` + `buildCamWb`; the plugin reports a Kelvin min/max. Flag-gated; device-pending. Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED.

**The camera menu gains a resolution row that changes with the lens.** The plugin reports a `resolutions` catalog `[{id,label,maxFps}]` — only the named sizes (720p / 1080p / 4K) the CURRENT lens actually offers, each with its max frame rate (a physical tele may not do 4K, so the options change per lens, exactly as Daniel wanted to see). [shell/native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js) tracks the chosen `preset` + `targetFps`, gained `setResolution`/`setFrameRate` (both re-acquire the session like a lens switch) and `getResolutions`/`getResolution`/`getFrameRate`. UI ([mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js)): under the lens row, a **resolution** segmented control (always shown when live); and in **record-video** mode a **frame rate** row (30 / 60, gated by the selected resolution's max). A shared `buildCamSeg` helper renders all three pickers and a shared `reacquireCamera` wrapper handles the re-acquire (drop any raw record take → re-point the engine → refresh the menu). Requesting a resolution clamps the pending fps to what it supports. Flag-gated; device-pending Daniel's per-lens read on the 14 Pro. **Note:** the still-opt/48MP lever was pulled OUT of this slice — it only becomes meaningful with the 48MP-still-on-pause path (wiring `capturePhoto` as the frozen source), so it moves to that slice rather than shipping a control with no visible effect. Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED.

**Two small fixes on the lens slice, and the branch's build counter caught back up.** The lens labels now use the proper **× (U+00D7) glyph** (`0.5× · 1× · 3×`) instead of an ASCII `x` — safe end-to-end (Swift UTF-8 source → UTF-8 JSON bridge → DOM `textContent`; it's display-only, never an identifier). The **flip-camera row** in the camera-settings popover ([mobile/styles.css](../src/mobile/styles.css)) was misaligned — its asymmetric padding sat the glyph high in the row; it now mirrors the proven `.m-menu-item` metrics (symmetric padding, flex-centered `.m-menu-icon`) so the icon sits on the text center line. **Versioning reconciliation:** the graduated native-camera slices (Builds 307–312 below) shipped real branch code but missed their build/version bumps (they'd been treated like the throwaway spike, which was wrong — only the spike harness is exempt). The counter is corrected here; going forward every branch increment gets the four-part standing maintenance. Native camera stays flag-gated behind `VITE_FOLD_NATIVE_CAM`, invisible to the default build. Verified: `node --check`, `vite build`, `xcodebuild` sim BUILD SUCCEEDED.

## v0.15.11 (Build 312) — 2026-07-12 — camera slice 3: physical-lens picker (drop "auto") in a camera-settings popover

**The discrete lens picker, and production now drives physical lenses only.** Dropped the auto-switching virtual composite entirely (it disables custom-Kelvin WB + 48MP; a single physical sensor allows both) — [shell/native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js) defaults to the physical `wide` (1×) lens and gained `getLenses`/`getLens`/`setLens` (setLens re-acquires the session like flip, resetting EV/WB to auto by construction on the sensor change). The plugin returns a `lenses` catalog `[{id,label}]` with **device-derived multiples** (0.5×/1×/tele) computed from the virtual device's `virtualDeviceSwitchOverVideoZoomFactors`. UI ([mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js)): a persistent **camera-settings popover** (the canvas-gear pattern) opened by a camera icon that replaces the flip icon on the native path — row 1 the flip control (relocated), row 2 a segmented lens picker (hidden on the front camera or a single-lens rear like the Air); the whole menu disables while recording (a flip/lens re-acquire would kill the take). The web camera keeps its one-tap flip untouched. Flag-gated; device-pending Daniel's label/switch check.

## v0.15.10 (Build 311) — 2026-07-12 — camera slice 2: flip / front camera

**Front camera + flip on the native path.** The plugin's `start` takes a `facing` (front = a single `.builtInWideAngleCamera`/`.builtInTrueDepthCamera` sensor, position `.front`); [shell/native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js) toggles facing and bakes the selfie mirror into the RGB canvas via a `uMirror` shader uniform, reporting `mirrorsInSource: true` so `captureFrame` doesn't double-mirror the already-mirrored native canvas; the lens catalog is position-aware. ## v0.15.9 (Build 310) — 2026-07-12 — native-camera: preserveDrawingBuffer (pause/freeze reads real pixels)

**Pause stopped blacking out.** The native frame source is a WebGL2 canvas, and `captureFrame`'s freeze `drawImage(canvas)` runs outside the render loop — so the context needs `preserveDrawingBuffer: true` (and `desynchronized` dropped) or the out-of-loop read returns a cleared buffer. [shell/native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js). Confirmed on the 14 Pro.

---

## v0.15.8 (Build 309) — 2026-07-12 — native-camera: static registerPlugin import (fixes the hung start)

**The native camera actually starts now.** A dynamic `import('@capacitor/core')` stalls inside the `capacitor://` webview, hanging `start()` before any plugin call — [shell/native-camera.js](../src/shell/native-camera.js) switched to a module-scope `import { registerPlugin } from '@capacitor/core'` (the spike had proven this static path works). Cost: `@capacitor/core` in a shared web chunk (~9.4KB gz), accepted for correctness. Confirmed live rear camera renders through the real engine on the 14 Pro.

## v0.15.7 (Build 308) — 2026-07-12 — native-camera: plugin-acquire via window.Capacitor (superseded)

**A first (wrong) attempt at the hung-start fix**, recorded for the branch's continuity: reaching the plugin via `window.Capacitor.registerPlugin` didn't resolve it (that global isn't exposed the way assumed) — superseded by the static import in Build 309. Diagnostic `start()` logging added here stayed.

## v0.15.2 (Build 303) — 2026-07-12 — native save reaches the phone: a host in the mobile chrome

**The iPhone chrome now has a native-services host too.** The mobile chrome doesn't mount `createApp` (it has its own lighter wiring), so it never had an `env.host`. [mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js) now resolves one directly — the Capacitor host in the native runtime, else the web no-op — and routes its `downloadBlob` (the save-sheet's writer) through `host.fileSystem` when available. So a save on the phone (still export, record-video take, package) opens the iOS **share sheet** instead of a browser download, which also dodges the WebGL-context-loss-on-save bug on the phone. Additive: on web `host.fileSystem.available` is false, so the browser download path is unchanged. **This host reference is the substrate for every future iPhone-native feature — camera controls, HDMI, NDI all read it.**

**Verified:** `vite build` clean, `cap sync`, `xcodebuild` BUILD SUCCEEDED, and the mobile chrome boots on the iPhone 17 Pro simulator (the capacitor-host import loads without crashing at init — its plugin imports are lazy). Runtime save is device-pending.

## v0.15.1 (Build 302) — 2026-07-12 — the Capacitor host substrate: native file save/share + preferences (iPad save now goes to the iOS share sheet)

**The iOS sibling of Electron's `window.foldHost`.** New [shell/capacitor-host.js](../src/shell/capacitor-host.js) implements the `shell/host.js` shape on top of first-party Capacitor plugins, so the app programs against `env.host.*` and never learns it's native — it just finds more services `available`. Plugins are **dynamic-imported inside the methods**, so the plain web bundle never loads them (they chunk into async modules that only resolve in the native runtime; verified the main bundle is untouched). Wired: `fileSystem.save` (writes the blob to app cache, then opens the iOS **share sheet** → Save to Files / Save to Photos / AirDrop — via @capacitor/filesystem + @capacitor/share) and `config.read/write` (native key-value persistence via @capacitor/preferences, the portable-config store's native backing). `externalDisplay`/`nativeCamera`/`ndi` inherit the webHost no-op until their Swift plugins land.

**Host resolution now covers Capacitor** ([main.js](../src/main.js)): `?mocksyphon` → mock; else `window.foldHost` (Electron); else the Capacitor host when `detectRuntime().isCapacitor`; else the web no-op. And the desktop/iPad save path ([source-host.js](../src/shell/source-host.js) `downloadBlob`) now asks `host.fileSystem` first, degrading to the browser download on web — so on iPad a save opens the native share sheet, and on native it **sidesteps the download-navigation that blacks out the WebGL context** (the parked mobile-save bug). Additive: on web `host.fileSystem.available` is false, so nothing changes.

**Verified:** `vite build` clean (async plugin chunks, main bundle unchanged); `cap sync` integrates all three plugins into Package.swift; `xcodebuild` BUILD SUCCEEDED; the app boots on the iPad simulator showing v0.15.1 with the plugins linked (no init crash). **Device-pending:** the actual share-sheet save + Photos write (needs a device / a save action, which the sim + no-camera can't fully exercise). The iPhone (mobile chrome) save path still uses its own `downloadBlob` — routing it needs a host wired into the mobile chrome (next).

## v0.15.0 (Build 301) — 2026-07-12 — NATIVE BUILDS milestone: camera-control foundations + the HDMI/NDI output seams

**The minor bump marks the native-builds milestone (Daniel's call).** Two additive foundations that the native passes build on, both verified by build (the runtime behaviors are camera/device-gated and verify on Daniel's device).

**Camera control foundations ([shell/camera.js](../src/shell/camera.js)).** The camera host gains a capability-gated control layer (his highest-impact lever): `capabilities()` (the live track's `getCapabilities()` — zoom range, torch, focusMode, whatever the platform exposes; recent WebKit adds zoom/torch/focus, older exposes nothing), `controls()` (current `getSettings()`), and `applyControls(obj)` (best-effort `applyConstraints({advanced:[obj]})` for zoom/torch/focus). Purely additive — no caller changes behavior yet; the camera-settings gear + the native plugin consume it. The layer keeps a reference to the live `track` (nulled on stop) so controls reach it. EV/WB/lens-select that getUserMedia never exposes come from the native shell via `host.nativeCamera`.

**The output seams ([shell/host.js](../src/shell/host.js)).** Two new host services, same no-op-on-web shape as the rest: `externalDisplay` (Capacitor watches for a second UIScreen and presents the chrome-free program view — output.html — on an HDMI/USB-C or AirPlay display while the controls stay on the device; a phone/iPad becomes a standalone activation broadcasting out) and `ndi` (publish the program output as an NDI network source Arena lists like a camera; native-SDK-only, mirrors syphon's publish shape). Nothing reads them on web (webHost stubs); the native shell fills them in.

**Verify:** default web build byte-clean (`vite build`); iOS build + boot unaffected. Camera controls + external-display/NDI behavior verify on device as their native plugins land.

## v0.14.22 (Build 300) — 2026-07-11 — CAPACITOR ARC opens: the iOS wrapper boots (build → boot → render → reuse, proven in the simulator) + the cross-shell EDITION gating seam

**Pass 1, part 1 of the Capacitor arc: the native pipeline is stood up and the forkability seam is in.** Two independent pieces.

**The cross-shell gating seam ([kit/capabilities.js](../src/kit/capabilities.js)).** Forkability is now a first-class, platform-independent lever, decided EARLY per Daniel's anti-rework ask. New exports: `EDITION` (a build-time flag Vite bakes from `VITE_FOLD_EDITION`, with a `?edition=` runtime override for testing the gates in a browser), `detectRuntime()` → `isNative`/`isCapacitor`/`isElectron` (engine-independent, from `window.Capacitor`/`window.foldHost`, so the phone chrome can read it without mounting createApp), and `editionAllows(feature)` over an `EDITION_FEATURES` map that DEFAULTS TO EVERYTHING-ON — this is the seam, not a paywall, so the shipping `web`/`desktop` builds are byte-untouched. The two axes are named: NATIVE CAPABILITY (`env.host.*`) vs EDITION/TIER (the same flag honored by web, Electron AND Capacitor, so a future "Electron + iPad bundle without motion" or a freemium mobile tier is one flag both chromes read). Both chromes read it: [main.js](../src/main.js) gates the mode picker (a withheld mode drops from the dropdown AND its hidden wiring button; `?edition=lite` hides motion + perform), [mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js) reads the same seam at boot. Verified: `VITE_FOLD_EDITION=iostest` bakes into the bundle and the default build has zero trace of it.

**The Capacitor bootstrap (proven build workflow, Daniel's priority #6).** `@capacitor/core`/`ios`/`cli` 8.4.1 added; [capacitor.config.json](../capacitor.config.json) points `webDir` at `dist/` (pure JSON, no TypeScript, honoring the plain-JS rule); one-command `npm run cap:sync` / `cap:open` / `ios` scripts wrap `vite build` → `cap sync ios`; `.gitignore` carries the generated native artifacts (the `ios/` PROJECT is committed like `electron/`, the web-copy + build outputs are not). The generated `ios/` project uses Capacitor 8's default Swift Package Manager (no Podfile), which sidesteps CocoaPods for the base app; CocoaPods 1.16.2 is installed anyway for NDI/camera SDKs that ship as pods. **Verified end-to-end in the iPhone 17 Pro simulator: `xcodebuild` → BUILD SUCCEEDED → install → launch → the mobile chrome renders natively (the "tap + to begin" empty state, split divider, tab bar) with zero UI fork.** Native portrait safe-area reads correctly single-counted (the known "doubling" bug looks PWA-specific) — the landscape + iPad safe-area polish is the next sub-pass, evidence-based off simulator captures + Daniel's device. **Verify (Daniel):** `npm run ios` opens Xcode on the project; on device it installs and boots to the same app.

## v0.14.21 (Build 299) — 2026-07-11 — gestures ACCUMULATE over autoplay (no cooldown, no pause) · the Capacitor arc capture. ARC CLOSED.

**Daniel's close-out nit, shipped as the better contract:** manual input now ACCUMULATES over the drift instead of interrupting it ([kit/drift.js](../src/kit/drift.js)). When a hand moves a wandering field, the whole spring frame (current, home, destination — velocity untouched) SHIFTS by the hand's delta and keeps breathing: while a drag is live the hand is authoritative each frame (its write lands after the drift's and the next shift absorbs it), and on release the wander continues seamlessly from the new placement. The 2s cooldown, the re-home pause, and B298's re-roll patch are all GONE — they existed to manage an interruption that no longer happens. Harness-verified: sampling every second through and after a full two-finger gesture shows continuous motion (rotation walking 268°→356° with zero flat windows) where the old model showed ~2s of stillness. Desktop perform INHERITS this (shared kit) — the original back-off-and-cooldown was the approved desktop contract, so if the live-set feel regresses there, say so and it becomes a per-shell option. **The arc capture (Daniel: all fixes confirmed, arc ready to close):** BACKLOG gains "▶ CAPACITOR ARC" under Native wrapper — the consolidated brief for his named next arc: the repo-resident workflow (Xcode only for signing + submission), the host-seam carry (`host.nativeCamera`/`host.ndi`, native permission persistence, native save paths likely dissolving the context-loss-after-save bug), THE first spike (camera control-plane vs data-plane: applyConstraints coverage vs AVFoundation frame-bridging — the real unknown), the WEB-side recording-resolution lever (offscreen second engine at record res + WebCodecs — available before Capacitor), and the AirPlay web spike (remote-playback API on a captureStream video) vs native-only NDI. **Verify (Daniel):** with autoplay on, grab any slider or gesture mid-wander — the motion should carry straight through your hand with no pause on release, on phone and desktop perform alike.

Autoplay + its sub-settings are increment 3b. **Verify (Daniel, on the phone):** gear top-left of the output panel opens canvas settings with the aspect row (16:9 re-tap flips to 9:16); slice sheet has the motion block with transition speed; set it slow, whip a slider, and the PiP + the recorded file trail the preview smoothly.

## v0.14.13 (Build 291) — 2026-07-10 — radial arc outranks the spoke · the phone's canvas zone becomes an output-frame proxy · the inputs surface enters the Lab

The canvas zone now mirrors the slice zone's pattern: the desktop pushes the output frame's aspect (`oa`), the phone draws an aspect-true FRAME CARD in the zone (circles + crosshair centered in it) and normalizes fingers to the card — they land 1:1 on the panel on any device ([remote-input.js](../src/shell/remote-input.js), [remote-page.html](../electron/remote-page.html)). **(3) The inputs surface is IN THE LAB** ([lab.js](../src/lab.js) "Inputs & settings"): sheet tabs, presence lights, device headers (connected/offline), mapping-row grid (cc/pad-with-LED/action states), drag + insertion-line states, and the finger echo drawn with its real styles — plus the DMG clean-install command (`xattr -cr`) and a releases-folder note in the CLI cheat sheet. **(4) The 40px icon-button discipline:** undo/redo/swap and all three panel gears now ride `.ot-btn.ot-icon` (all verified 40×40 with symmetric slack); the rule going forward is one icon-button component, new variants only for legitimate use cases. **Also filed in BACKLOG:** the generalized portable user-config file (rig + prefs + don't-show-agains in one versioned JSON) and the inputs-tab per-browser capability messaging (Brave shields block the Gamepad API — his DualSense datapoint; QR pairing is DMG-only by design). ## v0.14.11 (Build 289) — 2026-07-10 — the blank first frame, ACTUALLY fixed: the park was racing the thumbnail builder

**Daniel: still persisting after B288 — so this time the instrumented app told the whole story (tested with his real stock MP4).** B288's harness had validated the park in isolation; in the full app the park's seeks were landing at t=2.9s, 3.9s, 4.9s — because **buildSrcStrip (the frame-picker thumbnails, kicked off by updateSrcScrub at loadeddata) was seeking the SAME video concurrently**. Two drivers on one clock resolve each other's 'seeked' waits, every paint lands mid-seek (blank), and the strip's final restore-to-start repaints nothing — the panel stays black no matter how clever the park is (why B262, and B288's guaranteed-real seek, both "worked" in isolation and lost in the app; and why one scrub always healed it — a single-driver seek+paint). **The fix serializes the drivers** ([source-host.js](../src/shell/source-host.js)): the park yields all seeking while the strip builds, and the strip's finally-block — the LAST writer — now restores the clock and RE-PRESENTS (texture + render + panel paint + overlay), with the blank-probe and one forced re-seek as insurance. **Verified against his actual footage** (12902302-hd stock clip through the real file input): panel avg 0 → 120.9 from the first sample, stable, under BOTH autoplay policies (Brave-blocked and default). B288's guaranteed-real park seek + probe remain as the second layer. Fresh DMG. **Verify (Daniel):** fresh video load in Brave AND the DMG → the source panel shows footage immediately, every time, no interaction.

## v0.14.10 (Build 288) — 2026-07-10 — the Chromium blank first video frame: REPRODUCED, FIXED, VERIFIED · the seam seal moved into the shared drawer

**The pre-compress cleanup pass, both of Daniel's asks.** **(1) The Brave/DMG first-load blank video panel — finally closed with a measured repro.** Reproduced live in Electron (`autoplay-policy=user-gesture-required` = the Brave condition; H.264 injected through the real file input): source canvas painted pure black (pixel avg 0), and the state showed why — `played.length` was NONZERO even under blocked autoplay, so B262's park branch seeked to 0 with the clock at ~0.001s: a same-time NO-OP seek, and Blink never rasterizes a frame for drawImage/texImage2D from an occluded, never-presented video. The fix is structural, not inferential ([source-host.js](../src/shell/source-host.js)): the park now makes a GUARANTEED-REAL seek (target picked ≥5ms from wherever the clock sits) and then VERIFIES the paint — a new `sourceVideoBlank()` probe ([source-overlay.js](../src/components/source-overlay.js)) samples the panel canvas, and a blank result retries with fresh real seeks (capped at 3, so a genuinely black opening frame settles). ## v0.14.8 (Build 286) — 2026-07-10 — finger dots drawn IN the overlay pass; onion skins animate on the phone; lights + gear nits

**Daniel's round (affordances ✓, flicker gone, positions still off).** **(1) Slice-zone finger dots now draw INSIDE the overlay's own draw pass** ([overlay.js](../src/shell/overlay.js) `drawRemoteFingers`, riding both drawSourceOverlay exits like the onion skin; the adapter just sets `view.remoteFingers` UVs and schedules a draw) — same ctx, same just-computed geometry, so disagreeing with the outline is structurally impossible; the separate fixed-position layer (dpr/origin drift → "down and to the right") is gone for the slice zone, and the dot radius is proportional to the panel (~2.2% of the image width) instead of fixed-large. The touch REPLAY was already exact (its synthesized coords round-trip through the interaction's own `_geom` math), which is why manipulation worked while the old echo lied. **(2) Onion skins on the phone kept and FIXED** (his lean): they froze at full strength because the streamed overlay PNG only re-rendered on state changes — while ghosts are live it now re-renders every push tick (~10Hz), so the trail fades and follows like the desktop's, with one extra render after settle to wipe it. The borrow also nulls `remoteFingers` so your own finger dots never bake into the phone's image. **(3) Presence lights restyled to the output-traffic-light idiom:** 5px dots, pairs stack vertically, columns grow rightward — six devices reads as three slim stacks, one or two as one slim stack. **(4) The settings button is a standard COG** (the sliders glyph stays the panel-settings idiom). Fresh DMG. **Verify (Daniel):** slice-zone circles sit exactly on the outline where you touch, sized like fingertips; perform-chase ghosts on the phone fade and follow; two devices = one slim stacked light; the gear reads as settings at a glance.

## v0.14.7 (Build 285) — 2026-07-10 — finger echo registered via the overlay's own geometry; the flicker root-caused; TOUCH AFFORDANCES on the phone

**Daniel's reports (fingers under the wrong panel + flicker; touch affordances missing on the phone), all three root-caused.** **(1) Registration is BORROWED now, never re-derived:** the overlay publishes the image rect it actually drew (`sourceOverlayCanvas._geom`, wrap-local — the same numbers its interaction handlers read); the finger echo AND the synthetic-touch replay both map through it directly ([remote-input.js](../src/shell/remote-input.js) `sliceImageRect`). The old aspect/fit re-derivation didn't match the drawn rect — mispositioning everything, worse on smaller inputs since the error scales with the mapping (his phone-vs-iPad observation). Note: two-finger "working" never proved registration — the pinch handler ignores hit zones; single-finger inside/outside classification should improve markedly. **(2) The flicker was two writers:** slice repaints interleaved ~60×/s with the canvas-zone finger stream, which sends an EMPTY frame during slice touches — each clearing the whole layer. One finger store now owns it with per-zone entries. Canvas-zone echo is also aspect-true now (the phone sends its zone aspect; the desktop fits it centered in the preview rect). **(3) Touch affordances stream to the phone as the REAL overlay render:** the desktop borrows its own overlay drawer against an offscreen canvas with touch styling FORCED on (`env.forceTouchAffordances` — desktop is hover-media so `IS_TOUCH` is false there; [overlay.js](../src/shell/overlay.js) gains the override) and ships a PNG in the state stream (re-rendered only when the state sig changes, ≤10Hz; the WS framer gained the 64-bit length branch for >64KB frames). The phone draws that image over the gray card — outline, scale arrows, rotate arcs, and droste's arms handle, pixel-exact for every form, with the polys as fallback. Fresh DMG. **Verify (Daniel):** phone slice zone shows the full affordance set (switch to droste — the arms handle is there); circles sit ON the source panel exactly where touches act, steady; single-finger inside = move / outside = rotate classify reliably; canvas-zone fingers land unstretched in the preview.

## v0.14.6 (Build 284) — 2026-07-10 — the phone's slice zone IS the desktop overlay (synthetic-touch replay), direction fixes, unlock bar dropped

**The core capability lands the once-and-shared way:** instead of porting the overlay interaction to the phone, slice-zone touches now relay RAW (id + source-UV) and the desktop REPLAYS them as synthetic TouchEvents on its own source overlay ([remote-input.js](../src/shell/remote-input.js) `dispatchSliceTouch`, [remote-page.html](../electron/remote-page.html)) — so every behavior is EXACTLY desktop/iPad touch with zero duplicated code: single finger inside = move, single finger outside = ROTATE, the two-finger rigid-body (rotate + scale + reposition simultaneously — his core ask), droste arms/offset handles, edit-locks, undo/history, all of it, because it literally runs the same `setupSourceInteraction` handlers (raw touch events, no pointer capture — safe to synthesize; identifiers offset from real touches). The phone keeps drawing the streamed true outline; canvas zone keeps its delta gestures. **Direction fixes:** trackpad-over-source rotate and any contextual slice rotate now negate the screen delta (the overlay's Y-flip — the same negation the desktop two-finger handler applies; Daniel felt the inversion on both trackpad and phone); canvas rotation was already right and is untouched. **Slide-to-pause REMOVED** (his call: it was in the way; closing the tab + re-scanning the QR is the exit). **Finger echo:** 18px (~finger-pad; was reading as a giant cursor), and slice-zone echoes now ride the same UV registration as the touch replay, so where the circle shows IS where the touch acts; canvas-zone echo unchanged (maps onto the preview). ## v0.14.4 (Build 282) — 2026-07-09 — the DMG round: two root causes fixed + the mobile surface finished to spec

**Daniel's DMG test found the real bugs; both root-caused and VERIFIED fixed in a live Electron boot this session.** **(1) The everything-bug: `navigator.requestMIDIAccess` NEVER SETTLES in Electron without a permission CHECK handler** (verified: it hung a 4s race). The inputs-tab open handler awaited it before rendering — so in the DMG the mapping table never rendered, learn was unreachable, and the gamepad POLL never started (the DualSense read "connected" via the OS event while zero signals flowed). Fixed twice over: [electron/main.js](../electron/main.js) sets `setPermissionRequestHandler` + `setPermissionCheckHandler` (MIDI now RESOLVES — retested); and [input-bus.js](../src/shell/input-bus.js) renders FIRST, starting adapters in the background behind a 4s timeout race so no adapter can ever wedge the sheet again. **(2) The trackpad monitor never installed:** the addon deferred installation via `dispatch_async` onto the GCD main queue, which Electron's Chromium message pump doesn't reliably drain — the block simply never ran. The addon now installs DIRECTLY on the main thread (Electron main-process JS already runs there) and emits a `ready` event through the same pipe — verified live ([trackpad.mm](../electron/native/trackpad/trackpad.mm), rebuilt). **(3) The finger circles belong on the DESKTOP (spec misread):** the phone now streams its touch positions and [remote-input.js](../src/shell/remote-input.js) paints low-opacity circles into a fixed overlay across the Fold window (aspect-true centered mapping, stale-frame + disconnect clears) — eyes stay on the desktop; the phone keeps its local dots as peripheral confirmation. **(4) The phone surface is now TWO ZONES** (his original spec): slice / canvas split along the long axis (faint wedge glyph vs the crosshair-over-circles), each emitting its own drag/pinch/rotate signals (`mob:mobile.slice.*` / `.canvas.*`) mapped independently. **(5) QR pairing** (his dependency grant): `qrcode-generator` (MIT, zero-dep) renders the pairing URL as a scannable code beside the text. **(6) Devices are now removable:** ✕ on each device header deletes it + its mappings (confirm when maps exist; owned pad LEDs unpaint). Note: mappings made in Brave live in Brave's localStorage — `save rig` there and `load rig` in the DMG is the port path (the DMG then keeps its rig in userData). Fresh DMG cut. **Verify (Daniel):** DMG → gear → inputs renders instantly with the DualSense group + learn working; trackpad rotate/pinch map and move params; phone: QR scan connects, slice/canvas zones map separately, finger circles show over the DESKTOP app; ✕ removes a device.

## v0.13.3 (Build 277) — 2026-07-09 — ARC 6 OPENS: the CONTROL BUS — MIDI + game controllers through a learn-based mapping layer

**The input architecture's foundation, nothing hard-coded** ([input-bus.js](../src/shell/input-bus.js) new, [midi-input.js](../src/shell/midi-input.js) new, [gamepad-input.js](../src/shell/gamepad-input.js) new, [index.html](../index.html), [styles.css](../src/shell/styles.css), [main.js](../src/main.js)). **One signal pool + one mapping layer:** adapters turn hardware events into normalized signals (`midi:<device>.cc<ch>.<num>`, `midi:<device>.n<ch>.<note>`, `pad:<index>.a<i>/b<i>` — keyed on device NAME so mappings survive reconnects); user-assigned mappings route them onto continuous parameters (full slider ranges from the catalog) or transport actions (stage/take/cut/autoplay/play — dispatched to whichever mode owns them, same buttons the keyboard presses). **Three mapping modes:** `abs` (position → the parameter's range), `rel` (signed encoder steps), `rate` (stick deflection = velocity — the natural game-controller mode, auto-picked for axes). Invert per row. **The [input] app-bar button opens the admin sheet:** detected devices, the mapping table, and **LEARN** — press "+ map", move any hardware control, it appears with sensible defaults; every row re-targets/re-modes live and hardware activity flashes its row (the "which knob is this" read). **Pad LED painting (APC40 MK2):** note-signal rows carry a color swatch (tap to cycle a curated 9-color palette; velocity = color index over MIDI OUT); mapped pads paint on connect and unpaint on row delete. **The bus writes env.state exactly like a hand** — perform's follower chases it, staging isolates it, autoplay's ownership yields the touched field, broadcasts follow: zero downstream special-casing. Persistence in localStorage; a saved rig re-arms silently at boot (the MIDI permission grant is remembered). **Adapters testable TODAY in Brave/Chromium — no Electron rebuild needed** (Web MIDI + Gamepad API are plain web there). **Not in this build (by design):** the APC40 default profile (zone allocation is a session WITH Daniel — learn makes any layout in minutes meanwhile); keyboard-device capture (ACK05 — needs a capture-scope design so it doesn't fight app shortcuts); audio adapter + the additive 'pulse' mode (designed, see BACKLOG); the native trackpad addon (rides the next Electron packaging round with the node-syphon revert). Build + `node --check` + vite green. **Verify (Daniel, Brave + APC40/Xbox):** [input] → devices appear (MIDI prompts once) → + map → turn a knob → assign it to slice rotation → the output follows at the transition speed; map a pad to take, set its LED color, watch the hardware paint; map a stick to rotation in rate mode; reload → the rig re-arms.
