## v0.13.2 (Build 276) — 2026-07-09 — VIDEO SOURCES IN STAGE CHANGES (the Arc 5 close-out)

**The last Arc 5 item: staging now works on video sources** ([motion-runtime.js](../src/shell/motion-runtime.js), [output-engine.js](../src/shell/output-engine.js), [perform-runtime.js](../src/shell/perform-runtime.js), [output-window.js](../src/shell/output-window.js)). The v1 limit existed because one \<video\> can't present two times at once (the committed loop's frame vs your edit frame) — so **staging on a video forks a SECOND hidden \<video\> on the same blob URL, and that copy IS the committed clock**: it loops within the trimmed range at the retime rate exactly like normal playback (p derives from its presented frame, so the program's params stay locked to the footage it's actually showing), while the shared element stays yours to scrub, play, and edit against off-air. **The new `env.programVideo()` seam** ("the footage the audience sees", the sibling of programState) routes all three program consumers to the committed copy: the output bus's hidden engine (Syphon + record), the live PiP / third panel, and the output window's video clock (the popup now follows the on-air loop, not your edit scrubs); each one's mid-seek upload guard reads the element it's actually uploading. Consumers keep the shared element until the copy's first frame decodes, so the handoff never blanks. **The take blend stays params-only** (approved plan): when the staged preview isn't playing, playback resumes AT the committed position, so the footage carries straight through the take; when it is playing, **[▶ + sync]** is the tool that phase-aligns the two loops beforehand. A video is stageable with just 1 keyframe (the footage is the motion — tweaking kf0's params off-air is the VJ case; stills still need 2). **Guards that this unlock made necessary:** the clip editor's menu item disables while staging (its trim handles write to the SHARED clip mapping live, which would shift the on-air loop — the tooltip explains); a source swap mid-staging commits as a cut before the old blob URL is revoked; the force-exit path (camera start / source gone) now also ends an open staging as a cut (it bypassed toggleMotionMode's exit — a latent leak for stills staging too); retime speed changes apply to the committed copy as well. The mfStage video gate + its "needs a still source" tooltip are gone. Build + `node --check` + vite green. **Verify (Daniel):** motion on a video with keyframes → play → S → the live view + output window + broadcasts keep looping the OLD animation while you scrub/edit freely; pause and edit — the on-air loop never flinches; + sync then take → seamless; take while your preview is parked → the footage continues from the on-air position; cut/discard behave as on stills; retime mid-staging keeps both sides at the same speed.

---

## v0.12.15 (Build 273) — 2026-07-09 — STAGE CHANGES: live keyframe editing while the animation plays on-air

**Daniel's approved spec, built** ([motion-runtime.js](../src/shell/motion-runtime.js), [perform-runtime.js](../src/shell/perform-runtime.js), [index.html](../index.html), [styles.css](../src/shell/styles.css)). **Toggle "stage changes" in the ⋯ menu (or S) while a still-source animation has 2+ keyframes:** the keyframe set FORKS — the COMMITTED copy keeps playing to the live view and EVERY broadcast on its own clock (the programState seam grew a motion-staging branch), while motion.keyframes becomes the STAGED set you edit with every normal interaction (add/drag/delete/context menu/+gesture all just work — the fork is upstream of them). **The stage/live split reuses perform's panels verbatim:** the output panel relabels "staged" and the live view (PiP or third panel, same layout selector) shows the committed loop — perform-runtime lends it via `env.liveView`. **Two playheads:** the dimmed ON-AIR playhead rides the committed loop; yours stays the normal one. **His play/pause decision:** space (and the play button) drives the STAGED preview — the existing playback machinery IS that player since it renders env.state, which no longer feeds broadcasts while staging; the committed loop is untouchable. **The staging bar** (timeline's top-right): live "staging · N changes" counter + [take] [cut] [discard]. **T = take, the only commit key:** committed swaps to staged while the on-air output CROSSFADES across the discontinuity at the shared transition speed (smoothstep; the loop keeps playing through it; the blend outlives the staging UI). **Cut** = instant swap. **Discard** = restore committed (undoable; the bar + S prompt before discarding real changes). Leaving motion mid-staging commits as a CUT — staged edits are never silently lost. **v1 limits (BACKLOG):** still sources only (one video element can't present the committed loop's frame and your edit frame at once — a second decode path is the spec'd follow-up; the mfStage tooltip explains); ghost MARKER styling (hollow/dotted staged diffs, struck deletions) is the next increment — the counter ships now. Also this build (docs): Arc 6 scope updated per Daniel (trackpad multi-touch in; APC40 zone allocation + LED zone paint in; audio later), the mobile gesture-input MODE spec'd for Arc 7 with the pairing answer (the Electron app serves the input page + same-origin WebSocket behind a QR code — public-HTTPS pages can't open LAN ws:// sockets), NDI clarified as native-app-only (browsers can't speak it), and the node-syphon item flipped to "fix merged upstream — assess reverting to the published package". Build + `node --check` + vite green. **Verify (Daniel):** motion on a still with a few keyframes → play → ⋯ stage changes (or S) → live view + broadcasts keep looping the OLD animation while you edit; space plays/pauses YOUR staged preview only; move/add keyframes → the counter ticks; T → the on-air loop eases onto the new keyframes at the transition speed and staging exits; cut is instant; discard restores (and undo brings the staged set back); S with changes prompts; the ⋯ toggle reads on/off.

## v0.12.14 (Build 272) — 2026-07-09 — autoplay recalibrated to Daniel's found-good settings + tempered canvas framing

**His calibration (pace 5% · range 30% · variety 60% · smoothing 90%, at ~2s transition speed) sat at the extreme ends of two sliders — the curves are remapped so that feel IS the middle** ([perform-runtime.js](../src/shell/perform-runtime.js), [state.js](../src/shell/state.js), [index.html](../index.html)). **Pace**: default (50%) ≈ 5.2s between picks (his liked interval), floor ≈ 15s, ceiling ≈ 1.5s (the old ceiling's 0.3s chaos is gone). **Smoothing**: default (65%) ≈ his liked response, with silkier headroom above. **Defaults now**: pace 50 · range 30 · variety 60 · smoothing 65. **Canvas framing tempered (his "more enthusiastic than expected" note):** canvasZoom and canvasRotation wander at a fraction of range (0.3× / 0.25×) and canvasRotation now OSCILLATES around its autoplay-start home instead of momentum-walking — the walk belongs to the slice (full rotations are the show); the canvas is the frame and stays near where you set it. Docs: the "stage changes" spec gained his two-playhead play/pause decision (space plays/pauses the STAGED preview while staging; the committed loop is on-air and untouchable; T is the only commit key) and BACKLOG gained the **Arc 6 CONTROL BUS spec v2** (one bus + mapping layer; MIDI-first with APC40 zone reservation + LED zone painting; network gesture companion needs no native app; NSEvent trackpad addon rides the existing node-gyp toolchain; audio-reactivity is a future adapter into the same mappings; iPad→Arena = NDI on the native track). Build + `node --check` + vite green. **Verify (Daniel):** defaults out of the box ≈ your found-good feel; the slow half of pace/smoothing gives even statelier drift; canvas zoom/rotation breathe near their starting framing instead of seeking extremes.

## v0.12.13 (Build 271) — 2026-07-08 — autoplay tuning round 1: intent, momentum, the spring glide, four dials, stage/auto exclusivity

**Daniel's tuning notes, all five addressed** ([perform-runtime.js](../src/shell/perform-runtime.js), [index.html](../index.html), [state.js](../src/shell/state.js)). **(1) The jerk, root-caused:** the glide was MEMORYLESS — every new destination changed velocity instantly (why it needed seconds of transition speed to look right). The wander now runs a **critically damped spring per field** (the follower's proven math): velocity stays continuous across destination changes, so a new pick never jerks and an opposite pick decelerates through zero instead of snapping into reverse. **(2) Intent via biases:** **momentum** — rotation keeps its direction 78% of the time with sweeps never below a quarter of range (more full rotations, fewer startling reversals; non-angular fields keep direction 65%); **coverage** — scale picks lean LARGE and position picks lean home, so the drift spends more time on looks covering more of the source. **(3) The dials restructure — energy split into its two real controls:** **pace** (how often a new position is initiated — his requested speed slider) and **smoothing** (the wander spring's response — his "honest in-auto smoothing", independent of transition speed), joining range and variety. **(4) The canvas-zoom fight, root-caused:** the guardrail bounds clamped DESTINATIONS, so a manual zoom-out beyond them made every pick drag the value back inside ("invariably seeks right back") — the bounds window now stretches to include wherever a manual edit homes a field (the guardrail bounds auto's wandering, never the user); ownership detection also tightened to exact-write comparison (auto yields to ANY external change, including slow trackpad pinches). **(5) Stage/auto mutual exclusivity, his proposal:** each button disables while the other is active with an explanatory tooltip ("staging is available when autoplay is off — auto drives the stage continuously" / "autoplay is available when staging is off — take or cut first"); space/S/A guard to match. Build + `node --check` + vite green. **Verify (Daniel):** auto at default transition speed — no jerk at new picks, reversals ease through zero; rotations mostly continue their direction with full turns; zoom the canvas way out mid-drift — it stays and the drift breathes around it; pace and smoothing feel independent; stage and auto exclude each other with the explanatory tooltips.

---

## v0.12.12 (Build 270) — 2026-07-08 — perform AUTOPLAY ("drift"): hands-off wandering within guardrails

**Daniel's approved spec, built** ([perform-runtime.js](../src/shell/perform-runtime.js), [index.html](../index.html), [state.js](../src/shell/state.js), [main.js](../src/main.js), [styles.css](../src/shell/styles.css)). **Auto is another pair of hands on the same stage:** a per-field wander writes destinations into env.state exactly like user input and the follower chases as always — onion skin, sync dot, stage/take/cut, broadcasts all work with zero special-casing. **The [auto] toggle** sits in the perform footer's left cluster beside play (**A** toggles it), with its **guardrail dials in a gear popover** (the panel-popover idiom): **energy** (pacing of destination changes + glide speed), **range** (max distance from each field's HOME, normalized per field), **variety** (how many fields wander at once; the subset re-rolls every ~5–10s). v1 wanders **continuous fields only** (rotation/position/scale/canvas + droste/square fields gated to their forms); destinations clamp to conservative bounds (rotation wanders freely, it wraps). **Manual wins per field (his tension, the ownership model):** auto tracks what it last wrote — a mismatch means YOUR hand moved the field, so auto backs off (~2s cooldown), adopts your placement as that field's new HOME, and resumes breathing around it. **Staging pauses the drift** (the stage is the off-air workbench); unhold re-homes automatically through the same mismatch path. Dials persist in session; auto turns off with the mode. Build + `node --check` + vite green. **Verify (Daniel):** perform → auto → the look drifts, live chases at the transition speed; grab any field mid-drift → it yields, then wanders around where YOU put it; stage → drift freezes with the stage, edit off-air, take → resumes; dials change feel live; A toggles; range small = subtle breathing, large = exploration.

## v0.12.11 (Build 269) — 2026-07-08 — +gesture REDESIGNED to Daniel's model: one keyframe, winding kept

**The B267 miscommunication corrected (his round 2): a gesture is NOT a timing recording — it lands as ONE keyframe** that blends from the previous keyframe like any other; compositions keep their handful of keyframes and users interact with it as a regular keyframe. **What the capture adds is the WINDING — the headline benefit he named:** rotate 350° or 400° during the take and the tween into that keyframe travels the FULL amount, not the 10°/40° shortest path. Mechanics: the take accumulates signed angular travel per frame (`kf.wind`, [motion-runtime.js](../src/shell/motion-runtime.js)); the sampler ([tween.js](../src/kit/tween.js)) snaps the recorded travel to the winding class that lands EXACTLY on the keyframe's angle — so later edits to the angle keep the laps gracefully, and smoothing/looping work unchanged (the spline already runs on unwrapped angles). The keyframe inserts through the normal +keyframe pathway (same selection/auto-space/undo semantics; state restores to the armed look first so the commit-to-selected step can't write the take's end into the PREVIOUS keyframe). Winding survives undo ([history.js](../src/shell/history.js)) and the motion-JSON round-trip. A full 360° spin that ends where it began is a valid take (the winding IS the content). Arm/record ergonomics unchanged (G; press again or ~1.2s stillness). Timeline replacement, take-duration, anchored-timing, RDP simplification: all GONE. Validated against the real sampler in a scratchpad harness (6 checks incl. no-wind shortest path, ±350°, 400° = lap+40, stale-edit lap retention, 360-spin midpoint — all pass). **The smoothed translation-path capture (his "added value, lower priority") is spec'd in BACKLOG**, not built. Build + `node --check` + vite green. **Verify (Daniel):** motion → +gesture → rotate the wedge ~350° (or spin past 360°) → finish → play: the loop travels the full rotation into that keyframe; the keyframe reads/edits like any other; undo works; save/load motion JSON keeps the winding.

## v0.12.9 (Build 267) — 2026-07-08 — +GESTURE: record a manipulation as keyframes (the Arc 3 reserved slot goes live)

**The reserved [+gesture] button works** ([motion-runtime.js](../src/shell/motion-runtime.js), [index.html](../index.html)) — unblocked exactly as predicted by the perform substrate: every input path already mutates the one state object, so sampling state per frame IS the capture tap. **The flow:** press **+gesture** (or **G**) in motion → ARMED ("● armed"; playback stops, selection clears so edits don't write through) → your next manipulation starts the take ("● recording") → press again to finish, or ~1.2s of stillness ends it (the dead tail is trimmed; an intentional mid-take hold survives). The sample stream **simplifies via RDP over the normalized state metric** (FOLLOW_SPANS units, shortest-path for angles) to at most 24 **ANCHORED** keyframes — captured timing is the gesture's rhythm, so nothing auto-spaces — and the take **becomes the loop**: it replaces the timeline (undoable; confirmed when real keyframes exist), and **the take's real duration becomes the loop duration** (a video source keeps its locked clip-derived duration; relative rhythm holds). **Loop closure:** ending near where you began drops the closing sample — the loop's return to keyframe 0 IS the closing move. Discrete state locks to kf0 per the timeline invariant. Sub-400ms twitches and never-moved arms disarm quietly. Algorithm validated in a scratchpad harness (6 checks: linear collapse → 2 kf, corner retention, angular wrap-through-zero, keyframe budget, mid-take holds, closure detection — all pass; not committed per the no-test-infra rule). Build + `node --check` + vite build green. **Verify (Daniel):** motion → +gesture → swirl the wedge around for a few seconds → press again (or hold still): the timeline fills with anchored keyframes that replay YOUR move at YOUR pace, looping; G arms/finishes; a twitch does nothing; replacing an existing timeline asks first; undo restores the old keyframes. **Design defaults to react to:** replace-the-timeline (vs append), anchored keyframes (timing preserved), duration = take length.

## v0.12.7 (Build 265) — 2026-07-08 — the droste pass: true onion-skin shapes + the seam divider affordance

**Daniel's two-in-one droste pass.** **(1) The ghost-shape bug, root-caused:** droste keeps a schema-placeholder `buildPolygon` that returns the full OUTER CIRCLE, and the onion-skin drawer strokes whatever buildPolygon returns — so every droste ghost was a complete circle regardless of the arms count or inner ring. Forms can now provide **`ghostPaths(state)`** (an array of outline paths) and droste returns the TRUE sampled region ([droste.js](../src/engine/forms/droste.js), [overlay.js](../src/shell/overlay.js)): at arms=1 the full annulus (outer + inner ring, two paths); at arms≥2 the annular wedge with the twist-shifted inner arc and log-spiral sides (the same geometry the overlay's OOB probe walks). Polygon forms are untouched (buildPolygon remains their ghost). **(2) The seam divider affordance (the parallel-lane item + the "lost the rotation affordance on the Droste circle" nit):** at arms=1 a spiral-less ring is rotation-invariant on screen — rotating gave NO visual tell, and there was no way to drag from 1 arm to more (the boundary-line drag only exists at arms≥2). The overlay now always draws the **seam divider** at arms=1 (the straight radial line; with spiral active the existing spiral curve IS the seam) with a **double-line grippy** riding its middle (radial's spoke idiom, brightening on hover): it turns with rotation (the tell) and it's **draggable to fold the circle into arms** — the classifier returns the arms drag along the seam band, and the drag reference flips by π so the grab starts at arms 1 with no jump and folds upward (2, 4, ... 12) as you pull around the ring; dragging back unfolds to 1. Build + `node --check` + vite build green. **Verify (Daniel):** perform with droste → ghosts trace the actual ring (arms=1) / annular wedge (arms≥2, spiral bends the sides); still mode droste at arms=1 → the seam line + grippy shows, rotating visibly turns it, grabbing the seam and pulling around the ring folds into arms and back; the arms≥2 boundary drag behaves as before.

## v0.12.4 (Build 262) — 2026-07-08 — keyboard shortcuts always land (the slider-focus bug) + the Brave first-load blank panel

**The space/S/T reliability bug, root-caused (Daniel: "flawless once I press take in the UI, unreliable before").** The key handlers guarded against ANY focused `INPUT` — and every slider in the app is an input that KEEPS focus after a click. Touch the transition-speed slider (or zoom, segments, anything), and space/S/T died silently until something else blurred it; clicking take blurred it via the footer delegate, which is exactly why take "fixed" it. Now only real text-entry fields keep the keyboard ([perform-runtime.js](../src/shell/perform-runtime.js), [motion-runtime.js](../src/shell/motion-runtime.js)): sliders and buttons fall through to the shortcuts (a focused button blurs first so space can't re-click it), selects blur after use while performing, and entering perform clears focus so the keys work from keypress one. Motion keeps one native nicety: a focused slider still owns arrows/Home/End (precision nudge); everything else reaches the shortcuts. **(2) The Brave first-video-load blank source panel, root-caused:** Brave blocks even MUTED autoplay by default, so the park nudge's `play()` rejects — and the fallback parked with a seek-to-0 that was a same-time NO-OP (currentTime already 0), so the never-played video never PRESENTED a frame and Blink painted/uploaded blank. A never-played video now parks 10ms in — a REAL seek that forces frame presentation ([source-host.js](../src/shell/source-host.js)). Build + `node --check` green. **Verify (Daniel):** perform → drag the transition-speed slider → space/S/T immediately (no take-first ritual); same after touching any slider or button; motion space after a slider; Brave → fresh load → upload a video in still mode → the source panel shows frame one.

## v0.12.3 (Build 261) — 2026-07-08 — the broadcast-jerk fix (message-driven popup render) + round-3 perform adjustments

**THE PRIORITY: choppy broadcast-window playback during canvas/wedge transitions (Firefox worst, Safari/Brave better).** Root cause = the known "Firefox throttles the unfocused popup's rAF" item, newly exposed because perform makes continuous motion the norm: the main app streams buttery 60Hz state, but the popup only PAINTED on its own starved rAF. Fixed in [output-view.js](../src/output-view.js): **the state message is now the render clock** — every incoming state renders immediately (messages aren't throttled), with the rAF loop demoted to a 100ms fallback. This should fix Firefox outright and smooth the residual jerk elsewhere; the camera-vs-still gap (texture upload cost per frame) is the separate perf ceiling. **The rest of the round:** **(1) caret**, actually a caret now (solid triangle) — and the fly-away is fixed: `.ot-btn`'s hover/active set the `background` SHORTHAND which wiped + transitioned the image; the caret longhands are re-pinned in every state ([styles.css](../src/shell/styles.css)). **(2) Transition speed max 2s → 10s** for very slow transitions; confirmed how it works: the value is the follower's RESPONSE (time constant) and actual moves are perceptually normalized by the spring, so it reads as "how long a typical move takes" regardless of move size. **(3) Space/S reliability:** the mode select now BLURS after a switch (a focused select ate keys — native type-ahead on S jumped to STILL, space toggled the dropdown) and footer buttons release focus on click; note: after opening a broadcast window the OS focus is in that window — click back into the app (unfixable from here). **(4) The video time ruler returns** above the footer timeline, showing the **EFFECTIVE duration (clip ÷ playback speed)** so retiming visibly stretches the scale ([perform-runtime.js](../src/shell/perform-runtime.js) `renderPfRuler`; removing it was my mistake, not a decision). **(5) Reset canvas no longer touches frame aspect** (Daniel's model: canvas settings are sub-attributes of the aspect) — which also kills the mid-broadcast desync he hit ([main.js](../src/main.js)). **(6) Mid-perform source switches refresh the footer** (identity-guarded via `env.refreshPerformSource` from `arrangeSlots`): video→still no longer leaves a stale timeline, still→video gets its timeline + autoplay without a mode round-trip. **(7) The still-source center placeholder** (Daniel's suggestion, agreed — the engine-capture strip is NOT trivial): source thumbnail + `name · W × H`; the full current→staged tween strip moved to the Parallel lane. Build + `node --check` green. **Verify (Daniel):** the broadcast window during zoom/rotation transitions in Firefox — this is the one to hammer; caret sits still on hover; 10s transitions; space/S after touching the mode picker + footer buttons; video ruler shows duration and rescales with speed; reset canvas leaves aspect alone; source switches mid-perform refresh the footer center both directions; stills show the thumb + meta placeholder.

## v0.12.0 (Build 258) — 2026-07-08 — ARC 5 CORE: staged transitions (hold · take · cut)

**The staged-transition commit semantics land on the perform stage — the arc's minor bump.** A **transport cluster** opens the perform footer ([index.html](../index.html), [perform-runtime.js](../src/shell/perform-runtime.js)): **HOLD** freezes the live output on its last committed look — the target feed to the follower gates off, and the stage (the main output panel) becomes an **off-air editor for what's up next**, exactly the Arc 5 model (the PiP + broadcasts keep showing the held look; even a form change stays off-air until committed, since discrete state rides the target feed). **TAKE** commits the current stage once: the follower blends live → stage at **the shared transition-speed slider** (the one primitive, now doing the job it was built for) — and **stays held**, so you immediately keep building the next look off-air. **CUT** snaps live to the stage instantly (it also skips an in-flight ease while following normally). Unholding returns to continuous following. **The in-sync dot got the semantics HOLD requires:** it now measures live-vs-stage divergence directly (normalized per-field, shortest-path for angles) rather than trusting the spring's settle flag — a settled spring on a frozen target still differs from an edited stage, so the dot correctly shows amber while a held stage diverges (tooltip says "HELD; the stage differs"). The onion skin needs no special casing: a held live view is settled (no trail), and a take generates the trail across the blend. Build + `node --check` green. **What Arc 5 still holds for later:** the three-panel layout option (PiP stays the default per Daniel; the side-by-side option should ship with the layout toggle), saved next-up snapshot slots (a stage library), and PiP auto-dock polish. **Verify (Daniel — the staged workflow end-to-end):** perform → hold → build a different look (wedge + canvas + even form) while the PiP/broadcast hold steady → take → the live view blends over at the transition speed and you're still held; edit again → take again (repeatable); cut → instant; unhold → continuous following returns; the dot shows amber whenever the held stage differs and clears after a take completes.

---

## v0.11.5 (Build 257) — 2026-07-08 — output window matches the main camera's capture mode (the X-offset bug)

**Daniel's broadcast-offset bug (webcam, Firefox; X ~30% right, Y fine, all forms — preview + PiP correct, only the output window wrong).** Diagnosis: the output window opens its **own** capture of the same physical camera, and a second consumer of a device can negotiate a **different resolution/aspect** than the main app's capture (classic Firefox behavior). Slice coordinates are normalized to the source frame, so an aspect mismatch skews X while Y roughly survives — exactly the symptom. Fix: the camera payload to the window now carries the **main capture's negotiated dimensions** ([output-window.js](../src/shell/output-window.js) via `engine.getSourceSize()`), the popup passes them as constraints ([output-view.js](../src/output-view.js)), and `camera.start` accepts explicit ideal width/height ([camera.js](../src/shell/camera.js) — overriding the max-res ask, `ideal` so it can't over-constrain). Cannot be verified without a real camera, so this ships as the strong hypothesis: **if a STILL image also offsets in the window, the cause is elsewhere — report that datapoint.** Build + `node --check` green. **Verify (Daniel, Firefox + webcam):** broadcast to the output window → the wedge position matches the preview/PiP; then sanity-check a still image and a video file in the window too.

---

**Two more from Daniel's round.** **(1) The mode control is now a DROPDOWN in the app bar's center, by undo/redo** ([index.html](../index.html) `#modeSelect`, [main.js](../src/main.js), [motion-runtime.js](../src/shell/motion-runtime.js)): it shows the **current** mode instead of revealing all three all the time (the `.ot-select` pattern the camera picker established). Unavailable modes are disabled options (motion while live camera; motion/perform with no source). Under the hood the old segmented buttons remain as a HIDDEN wiring substrate the dropdown proxies — all the ordered mode-switch listeners (motion-runtime first, perform-runtime second) are untouched, and `updateMotionUI` re-syncs the select so a refused switch snaps back. **(2) Live PiP polish:** width 32→24% of the panel (min 120px), corners rounded to `--radius-2xl`, and the **in-sync dot now hides when in sync** instead of turning green — Daniel flagged that green competed conceptually with broadcast-active green; chasing = accent dot, caught up = quiet (his suggested option). Build + `node --check` green. **Verify (Daniel):** the center dropdown reads the current mode and switches all three (disabled entries where a mode isn't available); the PiP is smaller and rounder; the dot appears only while the live view chases and vanishes on catch-up.

## v0.11.3 (Build 255) — 2026-07-08 — the perform footer: video loops while performing, transport + transition speed together

**Daniel's feature gap: performing over a video loop is the most common use case, and there was no way to play.** A new **perform footer** ([index.html](../index.html) `#performFooter`, [perform-runtime.js](../src/shell/perform-runtime.js)) gives perform mode its own control cluster: **a video source now LOOPS while performing** (auto-plays on entering perform; the loop drives the stage each frame, target-state rendered per tick — the camera's live loop already covered live sources), with **play/pause** and **speed presets** (50/100/150/200%, `session.performVideoSpeed`, separate from motion's retime), and **the transition-speed control moves here from canvas settings** (Daniel: shimmed in there it was conceptually out of whack — perform controls live together). The still-mode frame picker hides while the loop runs and **returns when paused** (pick a frame mid-set); exiting perform parks the video (still-mode semantics). Footer show/hide refits the panels. Transport controls hide for camera/still sources (the camera keeps its app-bar record/pause). Build + `node --check` green. **Verify (Daniel):** enter perform with a video → it loops immediately and the kaleidoscope moves; performing over it eases as before; pause → frame picker returns, scrub, play resumes the loop; speed presets audibly/visibly retime; transition speed sits in the footer; exit perform → parked; camera + still sources show no transport.

## v0.11.2 (Build 254) — 2026-07-08 — perform fixes round 1: the spin bug, the full-transition onion skin, no browser PiP toggle

**Three from Daniel's first perform session.** **(1) The stuck-rotation bug:** rotating 360°+ queued every accumulated lap in the follower's unwrapped target, so the output kept replaying laps (visibly rotating long after the hand stopped — at slow response, effectively forever). [kit/follow.js](../src/kit/follow.js) now **caps the angular lead at one turn**: live following chases where you ARE, in your direction, at most a full lap behind — never stacked laps (Node-validated: a 3-lap spin at the slowest response settles in ~8s; unwrapped values also re-base periodically so they can't grow unbounded). **(2) The onion skin now traces the FULL transition** (Daniel's question — the old version aged samples out after 0.9s, which truncated a long chase to its last stretch, and it also STROBED on camera sources because the perform loop's ghost draw fought the camera loop's own per-frame overlay draws): samples now persist for the whole chase (capped at 28, graded oldest-nearly-invisible → newest-strong), the entire trail fades out over ~450ms on catch-up, and the ghosts are painted **by every overlay draw** (`view.performGhosts`, drawn inside `drawSourceOverlay` at both exits) so no draw path can wipe them ([overlay.js](../src/shell/overlay.js), [perform-runtime.js](../src/shell/perform-runtime.js)). **(3) Firefox's own picture-in-picture toggle is suppressed** on every video element (camera, loaded source, clip editor — `disablePictureInPicture` property + attribute): clicking it ripped the source out of the app into a browser-managed window ([camera.js](../src/shell/camera.js), [source-host.js](../src/shell/source-host.js), [index.html](../index.html)). Build + `node --check` green; all 12 follower checks pass. **Verify (Daniel):** spin the rotation several turns fast at a slow transition speed → the output finishes within ~a lap of where you stopped, no endless spinning, no flicker; a big quick move shows the trail across the WHOLE arc, oldest faintest, all of it fading once caught up; webcam source shows no Firefox PiP button.

## v0.11.1 (Build 253) — 2026-07-08 — the onion-skin ghost: the live output's trail on the wedge overlay

**Arc 4 increment 3 — Daniel's ghost spec, wedge-outline flavor.** While the live output chases your edits in perform mode, the source overlay now shows **where the live output is and recently was** as ghosted wedge outlines — traditional onion skinning: the trail samples the live position (~every 80ms), each sample **fades with age toward nearly invisible** (0.35 → 0 over ~0.9s), and the whole trail **dies out as the live output catches up** (no new samples once settled; aging clears the rest, then one clean redraw). Implementation: [overlay.js](../src/shell/overlay.js) gains `drawGhostWedges` (outlines only, low alpha, drawn over a fresh overlay draw — visually equivalent to under, no changes to the hard-won main draw path; the shared image-rect math is extracted into one helper used by both) and the perform loop ([perform-runtime.js](../src/shell/perform-runtime.js)) samples/fades/draws. **Known gap:** forms with bespoke overlays (droste's annulus) have no polygon to ghost yet — skipped, filed in BACKLOG. Build + `node --check` green. **Verify (Daniel):** perform + a slow transition speed → drag the wedge far: a fading trail of outlines follows the live position across the source, oldest nearly invisible; stop moving → the trail collapses into the wedge and vanishes as the dot goes green; instant speed → no trail; droste shows no ghost (known, filed).

## v0.11.0 (Build 252) — 2026-07-08 — PERFORM MODE lands (the minor bump: the live loop is real)

**Arc 4 increment 2 — the third mode ships end-to-end minimal.** A **perform** segment joins still|motion ([index.html](../index.html); the segmented control's radius rules generalized to 3). In perform: **your edits render to the main output panel immediately (the STAGE — what's up next), while the LIVE view eases toward them** through the B251 follower — every input path (sliders, scrubs, wedge drags, output gestures, undo) works with zero per-control wiring because the perform loop feeds the working state as the target each frame ([perform-runtime.js](../src/shell/perform-runtime.js), new). **The live PiP** docks over the output panel's top-right: a small canvas with its own engine (the proven second-engine pattern) rendering the follower's snapshot, labeled `live` with the first cut of Daniel's **in-sync affordance** (accent dot while chasing, green when live ≡ stage; tooltip says which). **Broadcasts show the live view, not your edits:** new `env.programState()` seam ("the state the audience sees") consumed by the output bus's hidden engine ([output-engine.js](../src/shell/output-engine.js)) and the GPU output window ([output-window.js](../src/shell/output-window.js)) — in still/motion it returns the working state, so **broadcasting from any mode works** (Daniel's requirement) and nothing changes outside perform. **The transition-speed control** (THE one primitive, later drives the staged blend-in) sits with the output panel's persistent controls: instant → 2s, live-applied, persisted in `session.performResponse`. Mode discipline: perform **accepts live sources** (unlike motion — performing on a live camera is core); save hides, output shows; render stays motion-only; the motion timeline stays motion-only; a video source keeps still-mode parking + the frame picker (scrub frames mid-performance; the frame cut is instant by design). Exiting perform hard-cuts broadcasts back to the working state. Force-exits when the source goes away. If a PiP GL context can't be created, perform still works (broadcasts follow); only the in-app live view is unavailable (logged). Deliberately NOT yet: the onion-skin wedge ghost (next increment), PiP drag/resize, hybrid perform-from-loop (parked in BACKLOG per Daniel). Build + `node --check` green. **Verify (Daniel — the first real feel test):** load a source → perform → drag the wedge hard: the stage snaps, the PiP eases behind it, the dot goes accent then green; crank transition speed to 2s and watch a slow follow chase your most recent input only; set instant → PiP mirrors the stage; rotate 350° by dragging → the PiP follows the way you moved; start a broadcast (window or rig) in perform → the DESTINATION shows the eased view while the panel shows your edits; switch modes mid-broadcast → output keeps working from every mode; camera + perform; undo mid-perform eases back.

## v0.10.69 (Build 251) — 2026-07-07 — ARC 4 OPENS: the perform follower primitive (kit/follow.js)

**Arc 4 increment 1 — the substrate everything else in the arc consumes.** New [kit/follow.js](../src/kit/follow.js) `createFollower`: the live output chases a continuously-updated target state instead of snapping to edits. Design per Daniel's kickoff answers: **perceptual ramp first** — implemented as a critically damped spring per continuous field, which delivers the perceptual property without needing an explicit clock scale (Node-validated: an 18× bigger move settles in only ~1.6× the time), is velocity-continuous under streaming gesture input (no restart stutter), and cannot overshoot. **Interstitial inputs are bypassed by construction** (setTarget replaces — a slow follow fine-tuning several params moves directly toward the most recent input). **Angles follow unwrapped**: target updates accumulate shortest-path deltas from the previous target, so streamed 0→350° travels forward the way you moved while a single jump takes the short way (both Node-validated). Discrete fields (form/segments/mirrors) cut immediately. API: `setTarget · jump` (hard cut, for take/cut later) `· step(dtMs) · setResponse` (the ONE transition-speed control, ~0 = instant) `· remaining()/isSettled()` — the last two exist for Daniel's **in-sync affordance** (live and staged showing exactly the same thing). `FOLLOW_SPANS` is the per-field state-delta metric that makes deltas comparable across fields. tween.js exports `angDelta` for it; pure kit (no DOM/timers, caller owns the clock). **Not yet consumed by any surface** — increment 2 (the three-panel stage with output-live as PiP, pulled forward from Arc 5 per Daniel) wires it. Validated in Node (11 checks: perceptual timing, winding both ways, snap mode, no overshoot, settle detection); validation script kept out of the repo per the no-test-precedent rule. **Verify (Daniel):** nothing visible yet — this build is inert substrate; verification comes with increment 2.

---

## v0.10.67 (Build 249) — 2026-07-07 — real footage frames inside the still-mode frame picker

**Daniel's "I'd imagined we'd actually render frames in the timeline element" — turned out cheap enough to build now** ([source-host.js](../src/shell/source-host.js) `buildSrcStrip`, [styles.css](../src/shell/styles.css) `.ss-cell`): after a video parks, one ascending seek pass paints ~square, center-cropped footage thumbnails across the picker (4–16 cells by track width), dimmed under the playhead line — the motion-timeline treatment. The key trick that keeps it cheap: the pass **never calls `engine.updateSourceFrame()`**, so the parked frame keeps rendering in both panels while thumbs build (no freeze/flicker machinery needed). Safety: single-flight; **cancelled the instant you scrub** (the scrub owns the decoder) and finished after the scrub settles; footage restored to the parked frame afterward; also builds on return to still mode if the video arrived during motion. Cells stretch with panel resizes rather than re-rendering (noted as acceptable; a re-render-on-resize can come later if it bothers). Build + `node --check` green. **Verify (Daniel):** load a video in still mode → thumbnails fill the picker within a second or so, playhead line rides on top, output stays on the parked frame the whole time; scrubbing mid-build stays responsive and the strip completes after you let go; enter/exit motion keeps it sane; a baked clip (clip editor) rebuilds the strip.

## v0.10.59 (Build 241) — 2026-07-07 — Arc 2c: still-mode frame scrubber (no autoplay) + source-info dedup

**Video sources stop autoplaying in still mode** (Daniel's universal-sources direction): a loaded video **parks paused at frame 0** and a **mini scrubbable timeline** under the source picks the frame to work with — deliberately no playback transport ([index.html](../index.html) `#srcScrub`, above the meta line). Scrubbing uses latest-wins seek coalescing (the `scrubVideo` pattern) so dragging never floods the decoder. One engine gotcha handled: a paused, NEVER-PLAYED video doesn't paint on Blink/Gecko, so the load nudges it (play muted → pause after the first frames present → seek back to 0). **Exiting motion mode no longer resumes free-run playback** — it stays parked on the playhead's frame with the scrubber shown. The scrubber hides during motion / live camera / frozen (synced via `updateMotionUI`). **Source-info dedup (Arc 2c):** the top-left caption no longer echoes `filename · dims` (or the resting "live camera") — the source panel's meta line is the ONE home, and a video's meta now carries **duration** beside the dims (`W × H · 12.3s`); the caption keeps only transients (starting camera…, captured) and errors. Build + `node --check` green. **Remaining 2c piece:** the fit/fill toggle (needs source-overlay component work — next increment). **Verify (Daniel):** load a video in still mode → parked (not playing), scrubber under the source, dragging picks frames smoothly and the kaleidoscope follows; enter motion → scrubber hides, timeline drives; exit motion → parked at the playhead frame, scrubber back; broadcast of a parked video is a stable frame; top-left shows nothing at rest, meta shows dims · duration · filename; camera flows keep their transient captions.

## v0.10.52 (Build 234) — 2026-07-06 — mobile restore fix, take 2: cache the lose-context extension (Arc 0)

**Why Build 230 didn't stick (Daniel's repro: still black after save):** the restore path looked up `WEBGL_lose_context` at restore time — but **on a LOST context Safari's `getExtension` returns null**, so `restoreContext()` silently never fired. Fixed in [mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js): the extension is grabbed once WHILE THE CONTEXT IS ALIVE and cached (`loseCtxExt`); both `pagehide`'s `loseContext()` and `onVisible`'s `restoreContext()` use the cached object (extensions stay valid across loss/restore cycles). **The live-camera case is different:** "start live cam → view download → back → BOTH panels reset" reads as iOS discarding the page entirely (a full reload — nothing to restore); that's the existing "persist the source across reload" backlog item (blob → IndexedDB), now cross-referenced there — not a context-loss bug. Build + `node --check` green. **Verify (Daniel, on device):** still → save → back → output intact; camera-frozen still → save → back → intact. If live-cam → save → back still resets both panels, confirm whether the page visibly reloaded (that's the persistence item, not this fix).

## v0.10.48 (Build 230) — 2026-07-06 — mobile: output survives the save handoff (GL context restore) (Arc 0)

**The "saving on mobile loses the output" repro — root-caused as self-inflicted.** Mobile's `pagehide` handler deliberately releases the WebGL context when the app hands off to iOS (the Safari GPU-context-pileup guard) — and saving IS a handoff — but nothing ever restored it, so returning rendered into a dead context (black output). Fix, both halves: **(1) engine** ([engine/index.js](../src/engine/index.js)) gains `reinitGL()` — rebuilds program/buffers/probe on the SAME canvas (getContext returns the restored same context object, so `engine.glContext` and every held reference stay valid; `engine.diagnostics` is refreshed in place to keep its identity) and re-uploads the current source. **(2) mobile chrome** ([mobile/chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js)): `webglcontextlost` → `preventDefault()` (required for restorability), `webglcontextrestored` → `reinitGL()` + resume (live loop or re-render); `onVisible` now asks for the context back (`restoreContext()`) when it returns to a lost context. Also covers genuine OS-initiated context losses. Desktop untouched (`reinitGL` exists but is only called by mobile). Build + `node --check` green. **Verify (Daniel, on device):** load a still → save composition → return → output intact; same with live camera running (camera resumes); same from the installed PWA (this was the [HIGH] triage repro).

## v0.10.47 (Build 229) — 2026-07-06 — keyframe ops enter undo history (Arc 0)

**Undo now covers timeline work.** History entries ([shell/history.js](../src/shell/history.js)) carry a **motion slice** beside the state copy — keyframes (per-kf copy; thumb canvases by reference, they refresh on the debounced filmstrip rebuild), selection, playhead — and undo/redo restore both objects together. New push points in [motion-runtime.js](../src/shell/motion-runtime.js): **keyframe add** (except the automatic kf0 seed on entering motion mode — a system add), **delete**, **anchor toggle**, **retime drag** (captured once, at the moment a press becomes a drag), and **motion-JSON load**. [main.js](../src/main.js) consolidates the four undo/redo triggers (buttons + ⌘Z/⇧⌘Z) into one `performHistoryStep` that stops playback before restoring (the tick would clobber it) and rebuilds the timeline surfaces (`renderTimeline`/`updateMotionUI`). **Scope note:** duration/loop/smoothing stay outside history (control-owned settings) — undoing a motion-JSON load restores keyframes but not those three. Build + `node --check` green. **Verify (Daniel):** add/drag/delete keyframes and undo/redo through each (markers + selection + playhead restore, thumbs refill after a beat); a slice edit between keyframe ops undoes in the right order; entering motion mode fresh doesn't create a weird extra undo step; ⌘Z during playback stops playback and restores.

## v0.10.46 (Build 228) — 2026-07-06 — Electron: keep broadcasting when Fold isn't the focused window (Arc 0)

**The Arena-rig blocker: selecting away to Arena paused Fold's playback**, making it impossible to drive Arena while receiving Fold's live Syphon feed. Cause: Chromium deprioritizes background renderers — rAF/timers throttle (or stop entirely when the window is fully occluded, e.g. Arena fullscreen over Fold), starving motion playback and the output bus. Fixed in [electron/main.js](../electron/main.js): `backgroundThrottling: false` in the BrowserWindow `webPreferences` (keeps rAF + timers + the Page Visibility API live while blurred/occluded) plus the process-wide `disable-renderer-backgrounding` switch. Confined to the Electron shell; the web build is untouched. First increment of **Arc 0** of the UX restructure → perform program (plan: `~/.claude/plans/i-m-previous-sessions-we-ve-indexed-frog.md`). **Verify (Daniel):** rebuild (`npm run build`, then `cd electron && npm start`), start a broadcast with motion playing, focus Arena (windowed AND fullscreen) → Fold keeps playing and Arena keeps receiving live frames.

**Docs (same session, non-code):** `BACKLOG.md` restructured around the new program — Daniel's 2026-07-06 design drop (Still|Motion mode discipline, global app-bar spec, panel-sibling overhaul, timeline rework, realtime/staged perform, mobile perform w/ audio) sifted into the triage + family sections, with the arc sequence in the Fold Live digest.

## v0.10.45 (Build 227) — 2026-06-21 — Lab token auto-discovery; docs trim + ARCHIVE.md

**The Lab's token catalog is now auto-discovered, not hand-listed.** New [src/lab-tokens.js](../src/lab-tokens.js) (`discoverTokens` + `groupTokens` + `TOKEN_GROUPS`) parses every `--name:` declaration straight from `tokens.css` and buckets each into a curated, ordered group (first match wins); [lab.js](../src/lab.js) renders the groups instead of the old `NEUTRALS`/`SEM_*`/`RADII`/… arrays. **Add a token to tokens.css and it appears in the Lab on its own** with a live value + usage `n×` count — no Lab edit. A new CATEGORY still needs one `TOKEN_GROUPS` rule; after that its variants are automatic. Anything no rule claims lands in a new **"unfiled"** section (the drift flag — renders + counts, but nudges you to file it). Pure string logic, no DOM/CSS import, so it's **Node-validated** (85 tokens discovered, all placed, 0 unfiled — matches the old hand-lists exactly, and now also surfaces the 6 control/state tokens — `--focus-ring`, `--dur*`, `--disabled-opacity*`, `--touch-target` — that were never shown). Icons + form thumbnails already auto-enumerate; components/text-styles stay hand-authored (a specimen's intended states can't be inferred). Also fixed the stale CLI cheat-sheet line that said the DMG ships the default Electron icon (it's wired to `electron/build/icon.png` via `mac.icon`). `node --check`/build green. **Verify (Daniel):** open `/lab.html` — token sections look as before (+ a new "Control / state" section); then add e.g. `--c-test: #f0f;` to tokens.css and confirm it auto-appears under accents with a `0×` badge, then remove it.

## v0.10.42 (Build 224) — 2026-06-21 — fixes from Daniel's testing: radial corner-join regression, stop size, selfie persistence

**Three from Daniel's review.** **(1) Radial regression (from Build 223)** — the corner-join `closePath` drew a stray straight chord across the radial wedge: its `outerEdges` is an OPEN arc (a chain of segments; the spokes close the shape), not a closed polygon. Fixed in [overlay.js](../src/shell/overlay.js): close the path ONLY when the chain actually returns to its start (`hypot(last.b - first.a) < 1.5`) — true for square/hex/triangle, false for the radial arc. The arc's interior segment joins still smooth via `lineJoin`; no chord. **(2) Stop icon too small** ([icons.js](../src/mobile/icons.js)) — the freeze square was 11×11; bumped to 16×16 (centered in the 24 grid). **(3) Selfie-camera persistence** ([chrome.js](../src/mobile/chrome.js)) — `startCamera()` hardcoded `camera.start('environment')`, so freeze → "go live" always reverted to the rear camera. Now a `lastFacing` is remembered (updated on flip via `camera.isFront()`), so go-live keeps the flipped (selfie) camera. `node --check`/build green. **Verify (Daniel):** radial wedge has only the arc (no stray line) + still verify the closed polygons everywhere; the stop square is bigger; flip→freeze→go-live stays on the selfie camera.

## v0.10.41 (Build 223) — 2026-06-21 — segment-overlay corner-join (isolated, revertible)

**The "rough corners" cleanup Daniel greenlit, kept ISOLATED so it reverts cleanly.** [overlay.js](../src/shell/overlay.js) `strokeEdges` gained a `closed` param: the slice boundary (`outerEdges`) is now drawn as ONE continuous path with `lineJoin: round` + `closePath`, so the polygon corners JOIN instead of leaving the butt-ended, unjoined corners the per-edge `moveTo`/`lineTo` produced. Spokes still draw per-edge (they're not a loop). Assumes the boundary edges are sequential (`e[i].b === e[i+1].a`), true for the slice polygon. The ONLY change is in `strokeEdges` + the one `true` arg at the `outerEdges` call — **revert = remove the `closed` branch + that arg.** `node --check`/build green. **VERIFY EVERYWHERE (Daniel — this draws the source overlay wherever it runs):** desktop slice manipulation, mobile, and the source-preview baked into motion renders; check all polygon forms (radial / square / hex / triangle). If any outline looks broken (lines crossing → edges weren't sequential there), revert as above. Droste draws its own overlay (not affected).

## v0.10.34 (Build 216) — 2026-06-20 — UI Lab: usage counter FIXED (CSSOM-free string parser, Node-validated)

**The usage counter, finally fixed + actually validated.** Builds 211 (`document.styleSheets`) and 214 (`?inline` + an owned `<style>`'s `.sheet.cssRules`) both relied on the browser CSSOM and silently returned nothing in Daniel's browsers — and I had only been checking the build compiled, not that it worked (I can't run a browser). This build removes the CSSOM dependency entirely: [src/lab.js](../src/lab.js) imports the three stylesheets as raw text (Vite `?raw` = the verbatim file) and parses them with a pure-string parser (`parseUsage` — extracts innermost `selector { decls }` rules via `/[^{}]+{[^{}]*}/`, which skips `@media` wrappers and matches the rule inside; records each `var(--token)` against its `selector · prop`). **Validated in Node** against the real CSS files (the same logic, the same text the browser receives): 73 tokens with consumers, `--text-2xs` → `.mf-time · font-size`, and the unused tokens (`--space-*`, `--focus-ring`) correctly `0×`. Since the browser runs identical code on identical text, it populates there too. `parseUsage` is exported for that test. `node --check`/build green. **Verify (Daniel):** reload `/lab.html` — the `n×` badges now show real consumers and `0×` flags the unused tokens.

---

## v0.10.29 (Build 211) — 2026-06-20 — UI Lab: live usage cross-reference (arc Increment 3)

**Increment 3 — the Lab becomes a usage instrument, not just a catalog.** Added live `document.styleSheets` introspection ([src/lab.js](../src/lab.js) `buildUsageIndex`/`walkRules`): on load it scans the actual loaded CSS, builds `token → {selectors that consume it}`, and hangs an `n×` badge on every color/type/radii/spacing token that expands (on click — progressive disclosure, no inline bloat) to the consumer list (e.g. `--text-2xs` → `.mf-time · font-size`). Computed from the real CSS, so it is zero-maintenance and always accurate; Lab-internal (`.lab*`) selectors are excluded so the Lab doesn't count its own usage; a cross-origin guard skips unreadable sheets. **A `0×` badge (warn-colored) flags an unused token — a candidate to cut**, which immediately surfaces the deferred-spacing gap (all `--space-*` read 0×, defined-but-unconsumed) and `--focus-ring` (0×, unused). This is the tool for Daniel's "reduce unnecessary in-between states" and "look up exactly where we use the 2xs style before deciding to kill it." **The CSS+JS span decision:** the CSS half is automatic/live; JS-referenced icons carry the grepped `ICON_USAGE` map from Inc 1 (accurate, no build step) — a fuller automatic JS scan would need a build step, deferred. `node --check`/build green; Lab additive/zero-risk. **Verify (Daniel):** `/lab.html` → click any token's `n×` badge to see its consumers; the spacing tokens + `--focus-ring` show `0×`.

## v0.10.26 (Build 208) — 2026-06-19 — design-system: standardize slider/scrub/button touch targets via --touch-target (Increment 4)

**Increment 4 — the controls converge onto one token-driven touch target; the only INTENTIONAL visual change of the whole arc.** The slider was styled twice with conflicting touch sizing: the desktop coarse rule set `input[type=range]` to 44px, but `mobile/styles.css` had `.m-control input[type=range] { height: 28px }` overriding it, giving the irregular, too-small mobile touch targets Daniel reported. **Fix:** removed the mobile override so the slider inherits the shared coarse `input[type=range]` rules from [styles.css](../src/shell/styles.css), and routed the coarse hit size through the new `--touch-target` token (44px coarse / 32px fine, with a `@media (pointer: coarse)` override in [tokens.css](../src/shell/tokens.css)). **Result: desktop-touch and mobile sliders are now identical (44px), edited in one place.** The same `--touch-target` now drives the coarse hit area of `.scrub` (min-width), `.ot-btn`, `.form-thumb`, and `.mf-btn` — all were already 44px, so that part is pure parity, just centrally editable now. **Visible change is mobile-only:** the settings sliders get a regular 44px touch target (was 28px); the visible track/thumb are unchanged, the row is just taller and easier to grab. **Buttons/scrub needed no other work** — Inc 2/3 already tokenized their color/radius/type, so the foundation is shared; the 40/48px mobile button sizes were deliberately left as-is (only slider/scrub touch targets are in the intended-shift scope). **Desktop parity re-proven** by the resolve-and-diff harness: still only the 3 Inc-3 collapse deltas + the `--font-sans` line — the touch-target tokenization moved nothing on desktop. `node --check`/build green. **Verify (Daniel — on device):** mobile settings sliders now have a comfortable, regular touch target (no more cramped 28px); desktop unchanged; editing `--touch-target` in tokens.css resizes every coarse control's hit area at once.

## v0.10.24 (Build 206) — 2026-06-19 — design-system: adopt tokens in desktop styles.css (Increment 2, parity-proven)

**Increment 2 of the design-system arc.** [src/shell/styles.css](../src/shell/styles.css) now CONSUMES the tokens: every color literal → a semantic alias (or a primitive where no clean semantic fits), every `font-size` → the type ramp, every `border-radius` → the radii scale, and the disabled `opacity` values → `--disabled-opacity`/`--disabled-opacity-strong`. **Strict parity, proven mechanically** — a resolve-and-diff harness expanded every `var()` back to its literal and compared against the pre-change file: **0 non-cosmetic deltas**, same line count. The only intended change is the body `font-family`, now `var(--font-sans)` (the conscious unification of the desktop `Helvetica Neue` and mobile `Segoe UI`/Roboto stacks into one superset) — invisible on Apple/Blink since `-apple-system`/`BlinkMacSystemFont` resolve first. **Left as literals by design:** the 13 `rgba()` alpha colors (overlays/shadows/translucent `.ot-btn` bg/amber-alpha clip region — no solid-hex token equiv), layout dimensions, transition durations, and spacing/gap/padding (a low-risk follow-up — the `--space-*` scale exists in tokens.css, just not yet consumed). New semantic added this pass: `--fill-bright` (the bright "primary" UI-element fill — primary button, slider thumb, scrubber, progress — distinct from bright TEXT). `node --check`/build green; the UI Lab now reflects the tokenized controls. **Verify (Daniel — parity checkpoint):** compare the desktop app against the prior build — nothing should shift (slice/canvas controls, app bar, output row, timeline, form picker, modals); then edit one semantic token (e.g. `--accent` or `--surface`) in tokens.css and confirm every consumer moves together in the app AND the Lab.

## v0.10.23 (Build 205) — 2026-06-19 — design-system foundation: token layer + UI Lab (Increment 1)

**Start of the design-system + UI Lab arc** (plan: `~/.claude/plans/in-a-previous-session-rustling-chipmunk.md`). UI INFRASTRUCTURE to de-risk future polish — not a redesign. The app had **zero design tokens on desktop** (`styles.css` hardcoded ~168 hex colors plus duplicated sizes/radii/type) and only a partial 6-token `:root` on mobile, so every polish/IxD change was a one-off hunt. Increment 1 is **additive and zero-risk** — nothing consumes the tokens yet, so the app renders byte-identically. **New [src/shell/tokens.css](../src/shell/tokens.css)** — two tiers: PRIMITIVES (`--c-neutral-950…0` ramp + accents + type/radii/spacing scales, faithful to every observed value so adoption can be pure parity) and SEMANTIC ALIASES (`--bg`/`--surface`/`--border`/`--text-dim`/`--accent`/`--ok`/`--danger`/… — what CSS consumes; edit once, every consumer updates). A `@media (pointer: coarse)` block overrides `--touch-target` to 44px. Linked in [index.html](../index.html) **before** styles.css; mobile reuses index.html's `<head>` (boot.js swaps the body), so the `:root` reaches desktop AND mobile. **New UI Lab** ([lab.html](../lab.html) + [src/lab.js](../src/lab.js), third Vite entry in [vite.config.js](../vite.config.js)) — a static gallery rendering every token (resolved live via `getComputedStyle`, so editing a token updates the swatch AND the printed value — the "edit once" proof) plus the core controls in their states. Reachable at `/lab.html` in dev and the built `dist/`. Build green, `node --check` clean, tokens bundle into both the app and the Lab. **Inconsistencies tokenizing surfaced (kept faithful, not collapsed — for conscious resolution): two record reds (#ff5a5a desktop / #e8504a mobile), two sans stacks (Helvetica Neue / Segoe UI+Roboto, unified in `--font-sans`), canvas backdrop #1a1a1a vs #111, ~4 near-identical dark surfaces.** **Verify (Daniel):** `/lab.html` renders all tokens + controls; edit one semantic token (e.g. `--accent`) → every consumer in the Lab updates; the app looks unchanged.

## v0.10.22 (Build 204) — 2026-06-19 — upload persists during live camera (switch source without dropping the broadcast)

Daniel's UX catch: while the live camera is running, the only way out was "stop camera," which clears the source and so tears down any live Syphon broadcast/record — you couldn't switch to a still/video without dropping output. Now the **upload button persists through live camera** ([source-host.js](../src/shell/source-host.js) `updateCameraUI`), sitting leftmost beside the capture/flip/stop group. Clicking it during a live broadcast loads the new source and keeps output alive: `loadImage`/`loadVideo` already exit live mode with `stopCameraMode({ keepSource: true })`, so the engine never goes sourceless and the bus/broadcast survives the switch (the upload control already accepts both image and video). Build green, `node --check` clean. **Verify (Daniel):** start a live-camera broadcast, click upload, pick an image or video — output switches to it without the broadcast stopping; the camera button still swaps for capture/flip/stop while live.

## v0.10.21 (Build 203) — 2026-06-19 — fix: camera-switch aspect stretch in the broadcast + DMG named with the real app version

Two from Daniel's DMG testing. **(1) Camera-switch stretch (the bug).** Switching to certain cameras (iPhone Continuity, Dell webcam — non-16:9 / renegotiating sources) made the Syphon/record output stretch vertically, while Fold's own preview stayed correct and the test pattern was clean. Root cause: `camera.js` reuses ONE `<video>`/mirror-canvas element across device switches and resolution renegotiation ([ensureVideo](../src/shell/camera.js)), so the element REFERENCE stays the same while its dimensions change. The output engine's source-sync only re-`setSource`d on a reference change, so the hidden engine kept the FIRST camera's `sourceAspect` and sampled the new camera's frame with the wrong aspect → stretch. (The preview is fine because the main engine re-`setSource`s on every switch; the test pattern bypasses the engine.) The MBP built-in (default-started, 16:9) never mismatched, so it didn't repro. **Fix:** [output-engine.js](../src/shell/output-engine.js) `syncSource` now re-`setSource`s when the source's DIMENSIONS change too, not only its reference (compares against `hidden.getSourceSize()`) — so the hidden engine's aspect always tracks the live source, like the main engine. Covers both camera switches and single-camera resolution renegotiation. **(2) DMG naming + one-command build.** The DMG was stamped `Fold Live-0.1.0-arm64.dmg` — electron-builder used the electron shell's `package.json` version (0.1.0, never bumped), not the Fold app version. New [electron/scripts/build-dmg.cjs](../electron/scripts/build-dmg.cjs) reads VERSION from `src/version.js` (single source of truth) and injects it, so `cd electron && npm run dist` now produces `Fold Live-0.10.21-arm64.dmg` (and re-applies the leak-fixed node-syphon binary + rebuilds the web app first — fully self-contained). `node --check` clean, build green. **Verify (Daniel):** switch to the iPhone/Dell camera while broadcasting — the output aspect matches the preview (no stretch); the rebuilt DMG is named with the current version.

---

## v0.10.20 (Build 202) — 2026-06-19 — hardening: graceful failure if the output engine's GL context can't be created

Hardening pass before moving to the next arc. The readback refactor (199) gives the output bus its own hidden engine — a SECOND WebGL2 context. If the browser can't grant it (context limit, GPU fault, WebGL2 unsupported), the broadcast/record would previously die silently: the bus caught the error, stopped, and the controls stayed lit with no frames and no explanation. Now the failure is surfaced. [output-engine.js](../src/shell/output-engine.js) `ensure()` throws a clear reason when the second `createEngine` fails; [output-bus.js](../src/stage/output-bus.js) records it (`lastError`, cleared on each `start()`), logs it, and exposes it via `getStatus().error` instead of swallowing it in the render-loop catch; [output-panel.js](../src/shell/output-panel.js)'s existing 500ms poll detects the dead bus (needs the bus but it errored and stopped), tears our side down cleanly (`failOutput`), and shows `output stopped: <reason>`. No behavior change on the healthy path. `node --check` clean, build green. **Verify:** normal broadcast/record unaffected; the failure path is hard to force on the M5 Max (the context succeeds) — primarily defensive for lower-end / context-starved machines.

---

## v0.10.19 (Build 201) — 2026-06-19 — fix: slice/output edits leak into the Syphon broadcast during playback

**Daniel (Build-200 smoke test):** dragging the slice while a video plays back made the **Syphon broadcast briefly show the wedge being manipulated before snapping back**, even though the edit doesn't take in the main app. Root cause: there was never an explicit lock on slice editing during playback — the main preview just *looks* locked because the playback tick (`startVideoPlayback`) runs `Object.assign(state, sampleAt(p))` every frame and re-renders, clobbering any drag before the preview paints. The drag DOES write `state` transiently, and the output bus renders `state` on its own independent loop — so it catches the uncommitted edit in the gap before playback re-asserts. **Fix:** a shared `isMotionDriven()` predicate (in [main.js](../src/main.js) — true while `motionRT.active && (playing || scrubbing)`, same shape as the existing `hideAffordances` gate) now locks the param-editing gestures on BOTH surfaces: the source overlay ([overlay.js](../src/shell/overlay.js) `onDown`/`onWheel` bail; threaded as `editLocked` through [source-overlay.js](../src/components/source-overlay.js)) and the output canvas ([output-gestures.js](../src/components/output-gestures.js) pinch/twist + trackpad-wheel — the same bug class, included so we don't ship a half-fix). The lock makes the restriction real rather than relying on the clobber, so neither the preview nor the broadcast shows the transient edit. Live camera and stills are unaffected (no animation driving state). `node --check` clean, build green. **Verify (Daniel):** play a video in motion mode and drag the slice (and pinch/twist the output) — nothing moves in the preview OR the Syphon broadcast; editing works normally when paused/stopped.

---

## v0.10.18 (Build 200) — 2026-06-19 — fix: Syphon broadcast flickers stray frames when pausing a long video clip

**Daniel's smoke test of the Build-199 refactor:** the perf win landed big (4K ~35-40fps, HD 100+fps, record less compressed + faster). One bug surfaced — pausing motion playback on a long clip (6-10 min) paused the main preview cleanly, but the **Syphon broadcast flickered through a series of different timestamps from the clip before settling**. Cause: pausing runs `stopPlayback` → `loadPlayheadIntoState` → `scrubVideo(playhead)`, which **seeks** the source `<video>` to the (keyframe-snapped) playhead; on a long clip that seek resolves slowly and the decoder presents a run of intermediate frames. The preview renders only ONCE (after the `'seeked'` await), but the bus's hidden output engine ([shell/output-engine.js](../src/shell/output-engine.js)) runs a CONTINUOUS loop and was calling `updateSourceFrame()` every tick — uploading each of those in-between decode frames. **Fix:** the output engine now skips the per-frame video re-upload while `env.sourceVideo.seeking` is true, holding its last settled frame until the seek clears — the same settled-frame discipline the preview follows. Covers the loop-around seek during playback too; the live camera (no `env.sourceVideo`) and stills (upload-once) are unaffected. `node --check` clean, build green. **Verify (Daniel):** broadcast a long clip in motion mode, pause — the Syphon output should hold the last frame and snap once to the playhead, no flicker.

---

## v0.10.17 (Build 199) — 2026-06-19 — output bus beats the readback wall (hidden engine + getImageData)

**The perf arc the Build-197 benchmark green-lit.** The live-output bus rendered the program to an FBO and pulled it back with `readPixels` — ~43ms for a single 1080p frame on ANGLE-Metal, the entire cost of Syphon/record (HD ~22fps, 4K ~5fps). The benchmark proved `drawImage` GL→2D + `getImageData` is ~9× faster (4.7ms vs 42.9ms), but that path needs the program on a REAL GL canvas drawing buffer (drawImage can't read an FBO) and we can't commandeer the visible preview every frame.

**Fix:** the bus now renders through a **hidden second engine** — the exact pattern the GPU output window ships at 120fps ([output-view.js](../src/output-view.js)), applied in-document. New [shell/output-engine.js](../src/shell/output-engine.js) `createOutputEngine(env)` owns an offscreen `<canvas>` + a lazily-created second `createEngine` + a 2D capture canvas; `renderFrameAt(w,h)` renders the live program there, `drawImage`s GL→2D, then `getImageData`. [fold-adapter.js](../src/shell/fold-adapter.js) `renderFrameAt` delegates to it instead of `engine.exportFrameRaw`. **Source-sync is trivial in-document:** the hidden engine shares the SAME source element the preview uses (`env.engine.getSourceImage()`), re-`setSource` on reference change and `updateSourceFrame` each frame for a live source (camera/video) — no second camera like the cross-document popup. Lazy creation means plain-web sessions that never output pay nothing.

**Orientation flips bottom-up → top-down.** `getImageData` yields top-left order, so the Frame now carries a `topDown` flag (+ an optional `canvas` passthrough); [engine-adapter.js](../src/stage/engine-adapter.js) documents both. Sinks honor it: [recorder.js](../src/stage/recorder.js) `drawImage`s the capture canvas straight in (drops its per-row Y-flip AND a putImageData copy — also speeds web record), [syphon-sink.js](../src/stage/syphon-sink.js) passes `frame.topDown` to the host, and [electron/preload.js](../electron/preload.js) + [electron/syphon-bridge.js](../electron/syphon-bridge.js) thread a `flipped` arg so Syphon publishes top-down with `flipped:true` (was hardcoded `false`). [test-pattern.js](../src/stage/test-pattern.js) now emits top-down too, so it stays a faithful orientation probe of the live path.

**Untouched:** stills (`exportAt`), video export, and the engine FBO/`readPixels` path itself (`exportFrameRaw` stays — the diagnostics benchmark still uses it; it's just off the live hot path). Build green, `node --check` clean. **Expected:** Syphon/record HD from ~22fps toward render-bound (~100fps+); 720p no longer the ceiling; web record faster too. Does NOT remove the ultimate IOSurface/native zero-readback ceiling — closes most of the gap with pure web tech. **Verify (Daniel, Electron):** arm the **test pattern** on the bus → in Arena "TL" reads top-left, "▲ TOP" points up, the circle is round, the red border is whole (orientation/flip correct); then broadcast a live 1080p kaleidoscope and check the diag op-ring `read` drops ~44ms → ~5ms and fps climbs; record a take (upright, high-fps); stills + video export unchanged.

---

## v0.10.16 (Build 198) — 2026-06-19 — non-swapped main wrap fills the stage (fixes Safari aspect; top-float still open)

The non-swapped main wrap used `max-width/max-height:100%` (shrank to the canvas) where the swapped branch uses `width/height:100%` + flex-center; [main.js](../src/main.js) `arrangeSlots` non-swapped branch now matches the swapped one. **Outcome after Daniel's cross-browser retest:** this **fixed Safari not honoring the wide aspect** (Safari now sizes the wide comp correctly with output on the right, like the others) — a real if unexpected win. **It did NOT fix the vertical top-float**, which Daniel now sees uniformly across Safari + Firefox + Brave + Electron (the 16:9 preview pins to the top of the main area with dead space below). So the top-float is NOT the `max-height`-vs-`height` thing I hypothesized from the screenshots — the static layout chain (`.ms-stage` flex-center → `width/height:100%` wrap → canvas; `.output-status-area` is `position:absolute`, not an in-flow sibling) *should* center, so the cause isn't visible from reading the code. **Next step (when revisited — Daniel says LOW priority):** live computed-style inspection — read the rendered height/offset of the `.slot-content` wrap and `.preview-canvas` in dev tools to see which box is full-height and where the slack actually lands. Build green, `node --check` clean.

## v0.10.15 (Build 197) — 2026-06-19 — readback benchmark + video-source blackout fix

**(1) Readback benchmark (the perf spike).** The diagnostics sheet has a new **benchmark readback** button ([diagnostics.js](../src/shell/diagnostics.js) `benchmarkReadback`) that renders 1920×1080 fifteen times each way and reports the GPU→CPU read: **A** `renderToFBO + readPixels` (the output bus's path, ~44ms on ANGLE-Metal) vs **B** `render + drawImage GL→2D + getImageData` (the engine's fast capture path, ~20× faster than readPixels on WebKit; Blink unmeasured). This settles whether the Syphon/record readback is beatable in-browser: if B wins big, an offscreen-canvas refactor of the bus is justified and HD could jump; if not, the readback wall is real and we accept the resolution constraint. **Run it in Electron and report A vs B.** **(2) Video-source blackout on swap — FIXED.** Daniel's repro: a video loop in motion mode, swapped so output is on the right, left the source preview + timeline filmstrip dark until you scrubbed or added a keyframe (every swap re-dropped it). Cause: a swap/relayout re-mounts the source view with a fresh blank video canvas, and only scrub/playback call `paintSourceVideo`. [main.js](../src/main.js) `arrangeSlots` now repaints the video frame + rebuilds the filmstrip (in motion mode) after the remount, so the relayout shows the current frame immediately. Build green, `node --check` clean. **Verify (Daniel):** the video-loop + motion + swap repro no longer goes dark; benchmark readback prints A/B times.

---

## v0.10.14 (Build 196) — 2026-06-19 — Electron: clear the PWA service-worker cache on launch

**Bug (Daniel): the Electron app was stuck on an old build** (showed Build 194 while the browser showed 195) and survived quit / force-restart. Cause: the built web app ships a **PWA service worker** (offline precache for the browser), and in Electron that SW kept serving its cached bundle, so a freshly rebuilt `dist/` was ignored. [electron/main.js](../electron/main.js) now clears `serviceworkers` + `cachestorage` from the session on each launch (before loading the window), so Electron always loads the CURRENT `dist/`. localStorage prefs (camera device, output destination) are preserved. **Consequence:** Daniel's earlier Syphon perf reading was on stale Build 194 — but the op-ring breakdown it captured is still valid and decisive (see below). **Verify (Daniel):** restart `npm start` → footer shows the current build; future rebuilds take effect on restart. (The DMG bakes `dist/` at package time, so this matters for the dev loop, not the immutable DMG.)

**PERF FINDING — the Syphon bottleneck is the readback, full stop.** The op-ring at 1920×1080 showed **`render 0 + read ~44 + publish ~2.3 ms`** (~20fps). So: single-render (render is already 0), zero-copy IPC and the backpressure relax (publish is 2.3ms) all save ~nothing — **the entire cost is `readPixels` GPU→CPU at ~44ms.** And since render is 0 (the GPU finished before the read), an async/PBO readback wouldn't help either (nothing to overlap). `readPixels` from a user FBO is just pathologically slow on ANGLE-Metal (~180MB/s for 8MB). The engine's *faster* capture path (`beginCapture`/`captureFrame`, drawImage GL→2D + getImageData — documented ~20× faster than readPixels on WebKit) commandeers the live preview canvas, so it's not drop-in for continuous broadcast. **Practical levers:** resolution is the real knob (720p ≈ usable; 4K is not), and a true fix (zero readback) needs the IOSurface/native path. See HANDOFF + BACKLOG for the corrected plan.

---

## v0.10.13 (Build 195) — 2026-06-18 — pinch-to-scale + Syphon backpressure + record bitrate

Three from Daniel's perf/gesture direction. **(1) Trackpad pinch-to-scale.** macOS delivers a trackpad pinch as a `wheel` event with `ctrlKey` (no real multi-touch on a Mac, so it's the one pinch that works on desktop incl. Electron). Wired on both surfaces: over the **source** it scales `sliceScale` ([overlay.js](../src/shell/overlay.js), same [0.05,10] clamp as the two-finger pinch), over the **output** it scales `canvasZoom` ([output-gestures.js](../src/components/output-gestures.js), [0.15,4]); one undo entry per gesture burst. (Rotation isn't exposed to Chromium/Electron via the trackpad — Safari-gesture-only — so that stays on the handle/controller.) **(2) Syphon backpressure relaxed 1 → 2 frames in flight** ([electron/preload.js](../electron/preload.js)). The strict one-in-flight gate serialized render and publish (no overlap); allowing 2 restores pipelining (the renderer makes the next frame while main uploads the previous) while staying bounded against the OOM. First of the wrapper-side fps levers; Daniel to re-measure HD. **(3) Record bitrate.** The recorder relied on MediaRecorder's default canvas-stream bitrate (heavily compressed); now targets ~0.2 bpp at 30fps (`min(40Mbps, w·h·6)`) for much better fidelity ([recorder.js](../src/stage/recorder.js)). Build green, `node --check` clean. **Verify (Daniel):** trackpad-pinch over the source scales the slice, over the output zooms; re-measure Syphon HD fps (op-ring `perFrameMs` shows render/read/publish split); a recorded take looks notably less compressed.

## v0.10.12 (Build 194) — 2026-06-18 — Firefox output-window sync + swapped mini centering

Two more from Daniel's testing. **(1) Firefox: output-window video sync now works.** The Build-190 reconcile ran only inside the popup's `requestAnimationFrame` loop, which Firefox suspends in an unfocused window — so the pause/scrub message arrived but never got applied, and the window's video free-ran while motion was paused. The reconcile now also runs on **message receipt** ([output-view.js](../src/output-view.js)), which isn't rAF-gated, so the video tracks the main clock even when the popup's render loop is throttled. (Firefox's separate ~1fps *render* throttle in the unfocused window is still open — tracked.) **(2) Swapped mini kaleidoscope now centers vertically.** Build 193's frame-aspect fix made the swapped-side mini non-square, which exposed that its slot never centered it (it floated to the top); the swapped side slot now flex-centers ([main.js](../src/main.js)). Build green, `node --check` clean.
